## Development Process in PDD Using Feature DB, DBT, Airflow

**Page ID:** 7652704454  
**Version:** 6  
**Last Modified:** 2025-11-27  
**Last Modified By:** Amit Choudhary  
**URL:** [https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/7652704454](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/7652704454)  

## Overview

This document outlines the development process followed by the Product Data Domain (PDD) team at Zendesk, focusing on the use of **Feature Databases** and **dbt** for safe, controlled, and efficient changes to our data pipeline.

* * *

## What is a Feature Database (Feature DB)?

A Feature DB is a dedicated Snowflake database instance created for development and testing changes to product data without impacting production or shared staging resources. It provides isolation for developers to:

  * Implement and test new business logic 

  * Add or modify columns 

  * Validate data correctness in a sandboxed environment 

  * Support User Acceptance Testing (UAT) by business stakeholders




* * *

## Creating a Feature Database Manually

Due to limitations with git commands and staging pipeline, **Feature DBs currently must be created manually** using [Zendesk Data Manager (ZDM)](https://datastores.zende.sk/ui/snowflake/sandboxes):

  1. Create the with naming convention __**SANDBOX** _<Feature_branch_name__Region> eg. __**SANDBOX**_ _FEATURE_CEAP620_AMER ( region is for refrence for UAT and Dev)

  2. Communicate with the business team to provide access to the Feature DB for UAT purposes. 

  3. Update the `profiles.yml` in your local dbt repo to point to this Feature DB under the designated profile, e.g.:


yamlwide760

Example   


yamlwide760

* * *

## Updating `dbt_project.yml` and Deploying Changes

When working in dbt repos:

  * Modify your `dbt_project.yml` as needed, for example ensuring appropriate tags (`staging`, `dev`) for models to control refresh behavior. 

  * For **backfilling or column additions** , you generally modify the model SQL, test in the Feature DB, and then **apply the**`staging deploy` label in the PR. This triggers deployment to the staging environment. 

  * Confirm the model refreshes properly on Feature-DB using DBT run and verify if airflow changes are looking good in Staging before requesting production deployment.




* * *

## Development and Testing Flow

  1. **Local Development:**

     * Build feature branch and run dbt models locally pointing to Feature DB (via `profiles.yml`). 

     * Run full refresh or incremental models as appropriate to verify logic.

  2. **Staging UAT for Ci/CD only :**

     * Push PR with `staging deploy` label. 

     * This step is for CI/CD check, Airflow deployment as we dont have access to Staging.

  3. **Production Deployment:**

     * After approvals, merge PR and create release on production repos. 

     * Monitor successful completion and data correctness post-release.




* * *

### Current Airflow Testing Approach

  1. **Airflow Job Completion Verification**

     * Primarily, the testing involves monitoring the Airflow DAG run to ensure it completes successfully without errors.

     * Check the Airflow logs to confirm that the DBT commands generated by the Airflow tasks are executed correctly.

     * Observe metrics such as runtime duration and resource usage during the DAG execution.

  2. **DBT Command Generation and Log Validation**

     * Airflow triggers DBT commands as part of its DAG tasks.

     * You can inspect the logs generated by Airflow to see exactly what DBT commands are being executed.

     * Validate that these commands align with the expected transformations and that no errors or warnings appear in the logs.

  3. **Data Validation**

     * Since the dev database access (which the Airflow staging environment points to) has been disabled, direct data validation in that environment is not feasible.

     * Instead, you take the DBT command generated by Airflow and execute it locally against a **feature database** environment where you have access.

     * This involves running the exact DBT command locally to deploy and test the transformations in the feature DB to validate data correctness.

     * Any discrepancies detected here are addressed before the Airflow DAGs are finalized for production deployment.




* * *

### Common Commands and Tips

  * Use `dbt defer run --select <models>` to run models selectively while deferring dependencies. 

  * Check DAG run times and schedules in Airflow for incremental/full refresh timing. 

  * Use `dbt_project.yml` tags effectively to manage model refresh behavior, especially for staging vs production deployments. 

  * Coordinate with business stakeholders for access provisioning and data validation on Feature DBs.




* * *

## Collaboration & Processes

  * Engage early with domain experts and product owners for clarifying requirements and design. 

  * Follow code review processes--add reviewers familiar with relevant product domains. 

  * Use Slack channels `#guild-dbt`, `#ask-zdp`,`#transform-product-data-curation-aggregate-foundational` `#ask-product-analytics` for help and coordination. 

  * Maintain documentation (README.md in repos, Confluence pages) for transparency and onboarding.




* * *

---

## Monitor Tool Overview (PDD)

**Page ID:** 7651655892  
**Version:** 2  
**Last Modified:** 2025-11-26  
**Last Modified By:** Amit Choudhary  
**URL:** [https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/7651655892](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/7651655892)  

## Summary

**Monitor** is an internal Zendesk tool designed to manage individual customer and test accounts, feature flags, and product settings securely. It provides engineering and support teams with a centralized interface to search, review, and modify configurations while ensuring compliance with operational policies and customer agreements.

* * *

# How Monitor Supports EDA CIO Use Cases

## 1\. Verifying Account Types (Active, Deleted, Sandbox)

Monitor's **Accounts tab** provides detailed, up-to-date metadata about each customer or test account, including:

  * Account status (active, deleted, sandbox/test)

  * Creation date and lifecycle info

  * Location of the account in terms of pod and shard




EDA CIO teams use this information to:

  * Identify which accounts are currently active and generating production data, ensuring analytics are run on relevant datasets.

  * Filter out deleted or sandbox accounts to avoid skewing reports or analytics insights.

  * Validate account status prior to running usage or behavioral analyses, improving data quality and accuracy.




## 2\. Tracking Recent Account Movement Between Pods

Monitor shows the pod and shard that an account currently resides on and the timestamp of creation:

  * Detect recent account migrations from one pod or shard to another (important for regional data compliance and localization).

  * Analyze movement patterns to assess impacts on latency, data synchronization, or service availability.

  * Verify that account migrations completed successfully without data loss or configuration mismatches, ensuring operational stability.




* * *

## Access

  * Monitor authentication is done via **Okta** combined with **VPN** access (required for production).

  * Access permissions are managed through Zendesk's **Sauron RBAC** system, ensuring role-based, secure, and compliant access to data and functionality.

  * By default, **all full-time Zendesk employees are provisioned access to Monitor** upon enrollment.

  * If you **do not have access** , or need additional permissions (e.g., ability to assume customer accounts or modify feature flags), you can request it by emailing [**_z2admin@zendesk.com_**](mailto:z2admin@zendesk.com) with your manager copied (CC'd).




### Production Monitor URL

[ _https://monitor.zende.sk/v1/accounts_](https://monitor.zende.sk/v1/accounts)

## Example: Verifying Sandbox Reclassification Using Monitor and Snowflake Data

To validate and understand the impact of the sandbox classification logic update (from subdomain-based to master_id-based), we cross-referenced live account statuses in **Monitor** with data snapshots from **Snowflake** (`DIM_INSTANCE_ACCOUNTS_DAILY_SNAPSHOT_BCV`).

### Key Observations

INSTANCE_ACCOUNT_ID| INSTANCE_ACCOUNT_NAME| Old Sandbox Flag (`IS_SANDBOX`)| New Sandbox Flag (`IS_SANDBOX_NEW`)| Monitor Status| Account Type (Monitor)| Active| Deleted| Trial| Trial Expired| Serviceable  
---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---  
25770512| testsandboxskuinstancere04| TRUE| FALSE| Suspended| Unknown| No| No| No| No| No  
25769986| [Sandbox Allowance Spec (Link)]| TRUE| FALSE| Active| Sponsored| Yes| No| No| No| Yes  
25428985| jeeny-sandbox| TRUE| FALSE| Expired| Unknown| Yes| No| Yes| Yes| No  
11169075| AutoBill| TRUE| FALSE| Active| Unknown| Yes| No| Yes| Yes| Yes  
12236204| CallRail Support| TRUE| FALSE| Active| Unknown| Yes| No| No| No| Yes  
20492346| Rauda AI SL| TRUE| FALSE| Active| Unknown| Yes| No| No| No| Yes  
  
### Summary

  * Many accounts flagged as sandbox under the old logic (`IS_SANDBOX=TRUE`) are **confirmed active, serviceable, and non-sandbox** via Monitor and new flag (`IS_SANDBOX_NEW=FALSE`).

  * The **new classification** accurately reflects that these accounts are **paid customers, trial accounts, or other valid statuses** , not sandboxes.

  * Instances labeled **expired** , **suspended** , or **unknown** in Monitor often correspond to legitimate lifecycle states rather than misclassification.

  * This monitoring and validation process helped identify and correct **overclassification issues** in sandbox flags caused by relying solely on naming conventions in the old system.




* * *

### How Verification Was Conducted Using Monitor

  * Accounts were searched by subdomain and ID in Monitor's **Accounts** tab to inspect current flags (active, deleted, sandbox).

  * Feature flags and configuration were reviewed to check for abnormal overrides.

  * **Account Assumption** was used where appropriate to review subscription and billing details confidentially.

  * Results were correlated with Snowflake's foundational dataset to pinpoint discrepancies and confirm the improved accuracy of the new sandbox logic. 




* * *

## Reference Links

  * Monitor Confluence Main Page

  * Slack channels for help: [#monitor-dev-collaboration](https://zendesk.slack.com/archives/CXXXXXXX), [#ask-monitor](https://zendesk.slack.com/archives/CXXXXXXX)

  * Monitor GitHub Repos and CODEOWNERS (internal links) 




* * *

## Important Info

**Description**|  The Sales Commissions & Attainment project provides comprehensive data assets for tracking and analysing sales performance, quota attainment, and commission calculations across the organisation. This includes foundational staging tables and production-ready functional tables for monthly, quarterly, and yearly quota performance analysis, as well as productivity and OTI (On-Target Incentive) tracking.

**Access**|  Internal stakeholders with ZDM Dataset Collection access - Sales Commissions Domain

## Commonly Used Queries

### For an employee_id get the quota_credit and quota_amount for specific period

sqlwide760

sqlwide760

### Employees who changed positions in a quarter  


sqlwide760

* * *

## Corner Cases & Important Notes

### Data Quality Considerations

#### Employee Leave Handling

  * `is_employee_on_leave` flag indicates employees on leave during any part of the period

  * Leave periods can span across month boundaries

  * Use caution when calculating averages to exclude leave periods if needed




#### Proration Logic

  * Commission proration is calculated based on effective employment periods

  * Mid-period hires/terminations are automatically prorated

  * Proration factors are stored at the employee dimension level




#### Currency Conversions

  * All commission amounts converted to USD using daily exchange rates

  * Original currency values preserved alongside USD conversions

  * Exchange rate source: Finance system daily rates




### Period Boundary Edge Cases

#### Fiscal Year Transitions

  * Fiscal year starts in February (FY25 = Feb 2024 - Jan 2025)

  * Some employees may have quota assignments spanning fiscal years

  * Use fiscal_year field for correct year attribution




#### Mid-Period Changes

  * Employee position changes mid-period are reflected in effective date ranges

  * Multiple records per employee per period possible due to position changes

  * Use `MAX_BY` functions for latest position information




### Performance Considerations

#### Large Dataset Queries

  * Monthly tables contain highest granularity and largest row counts

  * Use appropriate date filters to limit query scope

  * Leverage clustered columns (employee_id, period_name) for better performance




#### Incremental Processing

  * Functional tables use incremental strategy with daily refreshes

  * Historical data is stable; only current period data updates frequently

  * Full refresh recommended only for structural changes




### Known Limitations

#### Historical Data Gaps

  * Xactly system implementation started in 2023

  * Pre-2023 commission data not available in this system

  * Some legacy commission calculations may differ in methodology




#### Real-time Data

  * Data has ~24 hour latency from Xactly system

  * Intraday quota updates not reflected until next daily refresh

  * Use with caution for real-time commission calculations




#### Duplicate Handling

  * QUALIFY clauses used to resolve duplicates for specific currency pairs (JPY, BRL, INR) in 2017

  * Multiple position assignments can create duplicate records - use appropriate deduplication logic

---

## Model Deprecation in ZDP Guide

**Page ID:** 7538049537  
**Version:** 3  
**Last Modified:** 2025-10-16  
**Last Modified By:** Shubham Kumar  
**URL:** [https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/7538049537](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/7538049537)  

The Model Deprecation Guide provides a standardised process for safely retiring data models across the Zendesk data platform. Deprecating a model requires careful coordination to prevent unintended disruptions, maintain data integrity, and keep all documentation, alerts, and downstream dependencies up to date.

This guide outlines the essential steps and responsible stakeholder actions, including: auditing code repositories for active references, updating workflow orchestration (e.g., Airflow DAGs), managing metadata in Alation, notifying Data Stewards, adjusting monitoring alerts in Monte Carlo, and following proper Snowflake table retention and removal procedures.

Following this checklist helps ensure model deprecation is smooth, communication is clear, and our data landscape remains well-governed and future-proofed.

**Example:** `foundational.customer.fact_crm_opportunity_line_items_daily_snapshot`

* * *

### 1\. **GitHub Repository Audit**

  * **Identify usage:** Locate all production repositories leveraging this model.

  * **Revoke links:** Announce deprecation in slack channels such as `#zdp-announce` and coordinate removal of model references.   
**Example:**<https://zendesk.slack.com/archives/C08JC76MTV5/p1760454108325279>

  * **Current repos using this model:**

    * `zendesk/zdp_cloud_dbt_growth_analytics`

    * `zendesk/zdp_dbt_enterprise_data_ml`

    * `zendesk/zdp_cloud_dbt_presale`




* * *

### 2\. **DAG (Airflow) Update**

Determine if any Airflow DAG, tags (e.g., `crm_opportunities`) or hardcoded dependencies reference this model. Remove all explicit model calls and dependencies in Airflow code to avoid orphaned tasks.

* * *

### 3\. **Alation Metadata Update**

  * **YAML update:** Remove or update relevant [metadata in Alation](https://zendesk.alationcloud.com/app/table/26210/overview?sidebartab=details) for the deprecated model.

  * **Contact:** Coordinate with  for metadata and documentation changes.




* * *

### 4\. **Zendesk Data Store Update**

  * **Notification:** Inform assigned Data Stewards about the deprecation and coordinate any required changes.  





* * *

### 5\. **Monte Carlo Monitoring**

  * **Alert review:** Remove or update any data quality or anomaly alerts related to the model.  


  * **Contact:** Coordinate with the **Curation Team** for updates.




* * *

### 6\. **Snowflake Database Action**

  * **Retention period:** Retain the table for at least **2 weeks** after deprecation notice (unless otherwise specified).

  * **Admin tasks:**

    1. Request Snowflake Admin Team to drop the table from the master schema after retention. The below example script would be executed:

    2. Review and update any "FREEZING ASSETS" related to the model.




* * *

## PDD Development Cycle

**Page ID:** 7273317617  
**Version:** 12  
**Last Modified:** 2025-09-17  
**Last Modified By:** Vijay Jadhav (Deactivated)  
**URL:** [https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/7273317617](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/7273317617)  

**Product data domain is the information produced by the application and services Zendesk's offers and sells.**

Curation of which helps Zendesk in 

  * Improve product design and roadmap prioritization.

  * Enhance customer experience and support quality.

  * Drive revenue growth through better monetization strategies.

  * Optimize operational processes and resource allocation.




Detailed Analytics and Insights from PDD

  1. **User Behavior Analytics**

     * Track feature adoption and usage patterns across different customer segments.

     * Identify most/least used features or modules.

     * Analyze session duration, frequency, and user engagement metrics.

  2. **Customer Support Analytics**

     * Measure ticket volumes by channel, product, or issue type.

     * Analyze ticket resolution times and backlog trends.

     * Identify common customer pain points or recurring issues.

  3. **Product Performance & Reliability Analytics**

     * Monitor system uptime, latency, and error rates.

     * Analyze incident frequency and impact on users.

     * Track product version adoption and related performance metrics.

  4. **Customer Satisfaction & Feedback Analytics**

     * Analyze CSAT, NPS, and other feedback scores linked to product features.

     * Correlate customer sentiment with product usage or support interactions.

     * Identify drivers of satisfaction or dissatisfaction.

  5. **Churn & Retention Analytics**

     * Identify usage patterns predictive of customer churn.

     * Track retention rates by product version or feature set.

     * Analyze upsell and cross-sell opportunities based on product engagement.

  6. **Revenue & Monetization Analytics**

     * Link product usage to subscription tiers or billing data.

     * Analyze impact of new features on customer lifetime value.

     * Monitor trial-to-paid conversion rates.

  7. **Operational Efficiency Analytics**

     * Optimize support workflows using ticket and agent performance data.

     * Identify bottlenecks or inefficiencies in product usage or support processes.

  8. **Segmentation & Personalization Analytics**

     * Segment users by behavior, geography, industry, or company size.

     * Tailor product recommendations or support interventions based on segments.

  9. **Forecasting & Trend Analysis**

     * Predict future support volumes or user growth.

     * Identify emerging trends in product usage or customer needs.

  10. **Compliance & Security Analytics**

     * Monitor access patterns and data usage for compliance.

     * Detect anomalous activity that could indicate security issues.




**Setup and Access required for PDD Development**

  * Locally setup the repo (these are a few ones, will add more as will know)




git clone <https://github.com/zendesk/zdp_dbt_regional_support.git>

git clone <https://github.com/zendesk/zdp_dbt_regional_product_analytics.git>

git clone <https://github.com/zendesk/zdp_dbt_regional_talk.git>

git clone <https://github.com/zendesk/zdp_dbt_regional_guide.git>

git clone <https://github.com/zendesk/zdp_dbt_regional_user_entities.git>

git clone <https://github.com/zendesk/zdp_dbt_regional_dev_platform.git>

git clone <https://github.com/zendesk/zdp_dbt_regional_product_account_features.git>

  * Local setup of Airflow (For local testing, but we can even do Airflow Staging Workspace deployment, execute the DAG and test there as well) - <https://github.com/zendesk/eda_astronomer/wiki/Developing-DBT-DAGs>

  * **~~Deprecated (Can just remove this if required)~~**

    * ~~Raise request to get access to Snowflake Regional Accounts~~

[**~~WLLMI-2747 Snowflake Infra - Need DEV_DBT_ROLE to Region Snowflake Instance~~**](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/browse/WLLMI-2747?atlOrigin=eyJpIjoiNWExMGI4YTcyOTc4NGU0Nzg5YWEyYWNhZjhmZDMyNjAiLCJwIjoiamlyYS1zbGFjay1pbnQifQ)

  * Create a Shared Sandbox DB in AMER (Snowflake Production instance) through ZDM - <https://datastores.zende.sk/ui/snowflake/access> and request for access to the required stakeholders going to do the changes review and data UAT. This is the process to be followed if the changes to be tested are related to the business logic changes, where you need to compared/validate data against one of the Regional data on Production, like AMER production.

    *   * In VSCode (dbt core) product specific repo that you are making changes to, in that repo's profile.yml make the shared sandbox DB, role and WH specific changes to the 'local' profile as below:

    * dbt_container:

  outputs:

    local:

      type: "snowflake"

      account: "ZENDESK-AMER"

      warehouse: "{{ env_var('DBT_SNOWFLAKE_WAREHOUSE') }}"

      role: "SANDBOX_FEATURE_CEAP510_AMER_ROLE"

      user: "{{ env_var('ZENDESK_USERNAME') }}@zendesk.com"

      authenticator: "externalbrowser"

      database: "SANDBOX_FEATURE_CEAP510_AMER"

      schema: "dev"

      threads: 4

      connect_retries: 1

      reuse_connections: true

  * If you want to just do UAT in Staging environment, then deploy the PR to staging environment by adding the 'staging deploy' label in the PR. The default 'dev' config will be used in this case for loading the in the 'DEV_FUNCTIONAL' on AMER_STAGING snowflake instance. This kind of development and local testing is good for Structural changes, like adding/deleting columns. For loading data the ad-hoc doc available in the repo and on the Airflow Staging workspace (in this case 'Foundation Analytics Staging' workspace). 

    *   * If the DAG should be loading data on AMER_STAGING snowflake instance Shared Sandbox DB then in profiles.yml make the changes to the 'dev' profile entry after creating the Shared Sandbox DB through ZDM, as explained in above point. In this case, you need to temporary need to push the profiles.yml to the feature branch you are working on, but when merging the final PR with main, need to revert back to the default profile settings or main branch copy.




**Working in Regional Repos**

[https://lucid.app/lucidchart/e9a83c23-27ce-45e8-a3cd-35a50a6431f9/edit?invitationId=inv_e1e40f76-eec1-41c6-a10e-a503df5f83bc&page=0_0#](https://lucid.app/lucidchart/e9a83c23-27ce-45e8-a3cd-35a50a6431f9/edit?invitationId=inv_e1e40f76-eec1-41c6-a10e-a503df5f83bc&page=0_0#)

**Some Important Points to understand before developement**

  * Each ticket will contain the design document with the curation logic, source and target table/model name, granularity, if not please raise this in stand-up with Scrum master / Request owner. <https://docs.google.com/document/d/1sVCRNpirQHaPnClTtxQAdvHi7sUAig-92_BbbpY6WqE/edit?tab=t.0#heading=h.2fwmml4uyrt3>  

  * As only amer-staging is available, users can't UAT/test for different region data, so for small changes we deploy to production directly and ask users to UAT there after PR approval and deployment.

  * Better way is to tag 'Staging Deploy' label to the PR raised and then deploy the same to the Astronomer Staging Workspace and test the full refresh by manual trigger of amer-staging DAG, as on Staging we just have amer-staging available.

  * For new column addition changes to an existing table/model, will have to run the full refresh DAG on production before the scheduled run of the model's DAG on production for avoiding any schema changes related issue. The model changes should be pushed/merged to main branch and release created before full refresh DAG is executed. The full refresh DAG on both amer and emea needs to be executed.

  * For the initial version of code that is pushed to main, we need to raise a propagation request with Snowflake Admin, which is nothing but union of data from both amer and emea on the global accounts propogated_foundaational / propogated_functional. Reference - WLLMI-2693cae89f0e-c846-3d65-88a5-bb277a2031b3System Jira  

  * Update Alation with metadata like correct security and classfication and then field will be automatically available (it may already be in global but once alation sync then stakeholders/users will be able to see data). The details of the model for updating Alation is there in the design document available with the request. If not request Scrum Master / Request owner to provide the same. For Propogation we need to first finish the update of metadata in Alation. <https://docs.google.com/document/d/1sVCRNpirQHaPnClTtxQAdvHi7sUAig-92_BbbpY6WqE/edit?tab=t.0#heading=h.2fwmml4uyrt3>  

  * Check the main source model schema and try creating the propagated foundational / functional target model in that repo, for example, CLEANSED.PRODUCT_DEV_PLATFORM.BASE_ROLE_SETTINGS_SCD2 (source table), create the target model in <https://github.com/zendesk/zdp_dbt_regional_dev_platform.git> repo.

  * ⁃ Try searching for similar curated model available on any other PDD repos before starting the development, its possible same request is already made available in other repo by the different product teams. This happened as part of CEAP-447cae89f0e-c846-3d65-88a5-bb277a2031b3System Jira

none

## Supplemental Table level metadata

 _This table contains supplemental CRM attributes derived from Finance data: ARR bands, attributes based on ARR aggregations, etc.._

**Grain** : _The grain of the table is defined by the combination of_`crm_opportunity_id` _and_`service_date` _, resulting in one record for each CRM account per day_

**Table level filters applied** : _This table only contains CRM accounts that are found in the Health of Business pipeline. Customers with no billing data will not be represented here._

**Guaranteed data retention** : _This table is currently aligned with other HoB assets, which currently contain data from 2019 forward._

**Known data quality issues** : _This table contains some number of "synthetic" _`crm_account_id` values of the form `<source_system>-<billing_account_id>`. This method supports attributing ARR to a specific CRM account, even if it hasn't yet been mapped in Zuora.

 _Basic description of the data contained in the table can be found in Alation. This section contains additional column level information, that currently doesn 't fit into Alation._

## DIM_CRM_OPPORTUNITIES_DAILY_SNAPSHOT

**Page ID:** 7236386919  
**Version:** 3  
**Last Modified:** 2025-06-04  
**Last Modified By:** Suhas Jangoan  
**URL:** [https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/7236386919](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/7236386919)  

_This table level documentation contains additional user and maintainer facing information that cannot be easily captured in Alation._  
  
**Data catalog link**| [Alation](https://zendesk.alationcloud.com/app/table/21381/overview)  
---|---  
**Relevant analytic areas (see for common queries)**|   
**Pipeline Runbooks**|  _zdp_dbt_customer_foundational_  
**Other relevant docs**| [ _Opportunities Curation Document_](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1SunB9q033avONYZnCdXPiP9NGBFC45YP8F5xGuk7Jyc/edit?usp=sharing)  
[Stage3 plus date](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1E5mzijYFeB7nAqVaXrSiAhyaJPGsXYU4voaGI0OS404/edit?tab=t.0#bookmark=id.htb8tmeipf33)  
<https://docs.google.com/document/d/17EmW5UOcPQ-0WSLL94CGrOxf_opc05BrLCweGsodTq8/edit?usp=sharing>  
none

## Supplemental Table level metadata

The dim_crm_opportunities_daily_snapshot table captures daily snapshots of CRM opportunities, providing a historical view of each opportunity's status and attributes. Each record corresponds to a unique opportunity identified by crm_opportunity_id and source_snapshot_day, ensuring that users can track changes over time.

**Grain** : The grain of the table is defined by the combination of crm_opportunity_id and source_snapshot_day, resulting in one record for each opportunity per day.

**Table level filters applied** : The data in this table is filtered to exclude opportunities related to test or junk crm accounts.

**Guaranteed data retention** : This table maintains daily snapshots of data going back four rolling years. Older records beyond this retention period may be purged in accordance with future data management policies.

**Known data quality issues** : The fields OPPORTUNITY_IS_FINANCE_BOOKING and OPPORTUNITY_FINANCE_BOOKING_TYPE in the daily snapshot table are not fully reliable for identifying bookings because an opportunity's booking status can change, especially due to updates in the commissionable flag. Therefore, for accurate and consistent booking data and its attributes, it is recommended to use the fact_financial_bookings dataset as the authoritative source, since it reflects finalized and finance-validated bookings.

## Supplemental Column level metadata

 _Basic description of the data contained in the table can be found in Alation. This section contains additional column level information, that currently doesn 't fit into Alation._

### Business Logic Details

OPPORTUNITY_STAGE_NAME

**Stage Name Modification:**  
The OPPORTUNITY_STAGE_NAME is a curated field. On April 10, 2024 Opportunity Stage Names were updated in Salesforce. In this layer, all older Opportunity Stage Names are being re-mapped to the current valid list of Stage Names. This means that even in older snapshots of data you will see the latest Stage Names being used. This is so that no re-mapping needs to be done by the downstream users. The below mapping logic is applied:

`opportunity_stage_3_plus_date`

OPPORTUNITY_STAGE_3_PLUS_DATE

A date, of when an Opportunity (irrespective of whether this is a Renewal or not) has FIRST reached one of the below listed stages:

  * Opportunity has stagename in ('03 - Establish Value','04 - Demonstrate Value','05 - Secure Commitment','06 - Contracting','07 - Signed', '08 - Closed','Failed Finance Audit')"


OPPORTUNITY_BOOKING_MRR_USD & RELATED CURRENCY CONVERSIONS

These fields convert monthly recurring revenue (MRR), annual recurring revenue (ARR), renewal baselines, and forecasts from local currency to USD using currency conversion rates valid on the opportunity close date. If overridden values exist, they are used instead of calculated amounts. This standardizes revenue metrics for consistent reporting and comparison across currencies.

OPPORTUNITY_MEDDPICC_SCORE

This field sums together multiple MEDDPICC components related to the opportunity's qualification criteria, such as metrics, economic buyer, decision criteria, champion, competition, and paper process scores. If all these components are null, the score is set to null, else it returns their total as a float. This provides a single numeric indicator of the MEDDPICC qualification completeness or strength.

OPPORTUNITY_BILLING_PERIOD

Converts the opportunity's textual contract term length (like 'Monthly', 'Quarterly', 'Annually') into an integer number of months for easier numeric calculations. For example, 'Monthly' maps to 1, 'Quarterly' to 3, etc. This helps standardize billing periods across different term formats.

## DIM_CRM_USERS_DAILY_SNAPSHOT

**Page ID:** 7139754730  
**Version:** 1  
**Last Modified:** 2025-04-28  
**Last Modified By:** Shubham Kumar  
**URL:** [https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/7139754730](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/7139754730)  

This page contains a proposal for Table level docs for Foundational data domain. It also outlines what should live in Alation vs what would live somewhere in Confluence. The last two sections could either live on a single page in Confluence or the consumer and engineer facing docs could be separated into different pages.

\- field doesn't exist in Alation.

\- something exists, but not quite matches.

Note: for descriptions, we need to align on whether the team should be populating the Alation ones (rich text editor), or the DBT/Snowflake ones (plain text). Additionally we should evaluate whether more information could be parsed from code, including scheduling, refresh freq. etc. 

## Table level doc:

**Description** : The `dim_crm_users_daily_snapshot` table provides a daily historical snapshot of Salesforce CRM users, capturing their status and key Salesforce-specific attributes as of each snapshot date. Additional user details are sourced from Workday, enriching the dataset with comprehensive user information. Each record represents the state of a unique CRM user on a specific day, enabling tracking of user attribute changes and status updates over time. This table serves as a reliable source for analyzing user activity and status trends within Salesforce. To find more details and sample queries, refer to <link to confluence page>.  
  
**Grain** : The grain is defined by the unique combination of `crm_user_id` and `source_snapshot_day`. Each record corresponds to one distinct Salesforce CRM user's data captured on a single calendar day, including Salesforce status and Workday-derived attributes..

**Refresh frequency** : The data in this table is refreshed **daily** , with new snapshots added each day. Users can expect the latest available snapshot represent data for the last end of day business hours in UTC.

**History Tracking** : This table maintains **daily snapshots**.

**Data retention** : This table maintains daily snapshots of data going back **six** rolling years. Older records beyond this retention period may be purged in accordance with future data management policies.

**Known data quality issues** : if any.

**Additional analytics documentation & sample queries**: link to confluence.

## Column level doc:

**Pass through or derived flag** : Pass-through/Derived (_indicates whether the column is sourced from the previous layer without transformations or has been created through application of business logic.)_

**Description** : If pass through field, filled out by Alation. If derived field, describes the logic applied, if too complex to fit into short plain text description, refer to the dataset confluence page for more info.

**DQ checks applied** : e.g. not null, unique etc.

**Deprecation flag** : Can this column be used for new use cases, or is it scheduled to go away?

## DNU DIM_CRM_OPPORTUNITIES_DAILY_SNAPSHOT

**Page ID:** 7132282881  
**Version:** 4  
**Last Modified:** 2025-06-03  
**Last Modified By:** Suhas Jangoan  
**URL:** [https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/7132282881](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/7132282881)  

This page contains a proposal for Table level docs for Foundational data domain. It also outlines what should live in Alation vs what would live somewhere in Confluence. The last two sections could either live on a single page in Confluence or the consumer and engineer facing docs could be separated into different pages.

\- field exists in Alation.

\- field doesn't exist in Alation.

\- something exists, but not quite matches.

Note: for descriptions, we need to align on whether the team should be populating the Alation ones (rich text editor), or the DBT/Snowflake ones (plain text). Additionally we should evaluate whether more information could be parsed from code, including scheduling, refresh freq. etc. 

## Table level doc:

**Description** : The `dim_crm_opportunities_daily_snapshot` table captures daily snapshots of CRM opportunities, providing a historical view of each opportunity's status and attributes. Each record corresponds to a unique opportunity identified by `crm_opportunity_id` and `source_snapshot_day`, ensuring that users can track changes over time. To find more details and sample queries, refer to <link to confluence page>.

**Grain** : The grain of the table is defined by the combination of `crm_opportunity_id` and `source_snapshot_day`, resulting in one record for each opportunity per day.

**Table level filters applied** : The data in this table is filtered to exclude opportunities related to test or junk crm accounts.

**Refresh frequency** : The data in this table is refreshed **daily** , with new snapshots added each day. Users can expect the latest available snapshot represent data for the last end of day business hours in UTC.

**History Tracking** : This table maintains **daily snapshots**.

**Data retention** : This table maintains daily snapshots of data going back **four** rolling years. Older records beyond this retention period may be purged in accordance with future data management policies.

**Known data quality issues** : if any.

**Additional analytics documentation & sample queries**: link to confluence.

## Column level doc:

**Pass through or derived flag** : Pass-through/Derived (_indicates whether the column is sourced from the previous layer without transformations or has been created through application of business logic.)_

**Description** : If pass through field, filled out by Alation. If derived field, describes the logic applied, if too complex to fit into short plain text description, refer to the dataset confluence page for more info.

**DQ checks applied** : e.g. not null, unique etc.

**Deprecation flag** : Can this column be used for new use cases, or is it scheduled to go away? (part of schema change management process). E.g. for Opportunity `is_finance_booking` and `opportunity_freeze_date` is going to be deprecated soon, and shouldn't be used anymore.

## **Business logic details**

**Stage Name Modification** : The `OPPORTUNITY_STAGE_NAME` is a curated field. On April 10, 2024 Opportunity Stage Names were updated in Salesforce. In this layer, all older Opportunity Stage Names are being re-mapped to the current valid list of Stage Names. This means that even in older snapshots of data you will see the latest Stage Names being used. This is so that no re-mapping needs to be done by the downstream users. ## archive - DIM_CRM_OPPORTUNITIES_DAILY_SNAPSHOT

**Page ID:** 7061864772  
**Version:** 7  
**Last Modified:** 2025-06-03  
**Last Modified By:** Suhas Jangoan  
**URL:** [https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/7061864772](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/7061864772)  

### Description: 

The `dim_crm_opportunities_daily_snapshot` table captures daily snapshots of CRM opportunities, providing a historical view of each opportunity's status and attributes. Each record corresponds to a unique opportunity identified by `crm_opportunity_id` and `source_snapshot_day`, ensuring that users can track changes over time.

### Grain: 

  * **Primary Grain** : The primary grain of the table is defined by the combination of `crm_opportunity_id` and `source_snapshot_day`, resulting in one record for each opportunity per day.

  * **Other Available Grains** :

    * DIM_CRM_OPPORTUNITIES_MONTHLY_SNAPSHOT: This grain contains the last available daily snapshot for each opportunity at the end of the month.

    * DIM_CRM_OPPORTUNITIES_DAILY_SNAPSHOT_BCV: This grain holds the latest daily snapshot for each opportunity, providing the most up-to-date information.




#### Data Freshness

  * The data in this table is refreshed daily, with new snapshots added each day. Users can expect the latest available snapshot represent data for the last end of day business hours in UTC.




#### History Tracking

 _\--open for discussion_

  * This table maintains daily snapshots of data going back **four** rolling years. Currently, there is no process in place to retire old snapshots; however, plans for automatic retirement of older snapshots are being considered for future implementation.




#### Data Retention

  * This table maintains daily snapshots of data going back **four** rolling years. Older records beyond this retention period may be purged in accordance with future data management policies.




#### Data Quality Checks

  * There cannot be any null values for `crm_opportunity_id` on any given date. This guarantees that each snapshot is associated with a valid opportunity. 

  * Certain columns have not null/ unique and can be found in the mapping document.




**Table level filters applied** : 

  * The data in this table is filtered to exclude opportunities related to test or junk crm accounts.




**Source to Target mapping table**

  * For a detailed mapping of the table columns and their metadata, please refer to the [_Source to Target Mapping Spreadsheet_](https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1Rs6eqaj7UJWmFuQTAeXaecaXUql-zF1Zuqxc_yeVtmg/edit?gid=1536182136#gid=1536182136).




**Description of more complex logic/concepts**

  * **Stage Name Modification** : The stage name associated with each opportunity is subject to modification based on specific business rules. Details regarding these modifications, including the criteria and process for changing stage names, can be provided upon request or documented separately. This mapping is applied to the whole history, add github link. 

  * **Formula Fields - not needed**




**ERD - n/a for dimension tables**

**Sample queries**

**Known data quality issues**

  *  _\--open for discussion_

    * low data quality because we dont refresh the flags and should be removed.

    * is_finance_booking

    * opportunity_freeze_date




**Reference documents**

  * dimensional data modeling document

  * monthly_snapshot/daily_snapshot




**Change/decision log:**

  * **Initial design doc -**<https://docs.google.com/document/d/1SunB9q033avONYZnCdXPiP9NGBFC45YP8F5xGuk7Jyc/edit?usp=sharing>

  * **Any modifications (JIRA ticket links, RFC links, etc);**

    * Why are we making the change

      * What is the change

    * Who requested the change

    * Who signed off on the change

## Salesforce Formula Fields in ZDP

**Page ID:** 6834094500  
**Version:** 2  
**Last Modified:** 2025-02-06  
**Last Modified By:** Abdalla Zidan (Deactivated)  
**URL:** [https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/6834094500](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/6834094500)

**Team**|

At Zendesk, Salesforce formula fields are being used by different domain teams as part of data curation & enrichment. ## To retrieve Compiled/run DBT codes from DAG run on    Amazon S3

**Page ID:** 6794444858  
**Version:** 1  
**Last Modified:** 2025-01-16  
**Last Modified By:** Kumudini Chaudhari (Deactivated)  
**URL:** [https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/6794444858](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/6794444858)  

** _To retrieve Compiled/run DBT codes from DAG run on Amazon S3_**  
  
**Description:**

To understand the behaviour of DBT codes, post a DAG run in the Production environment and go back in time and get the compiled/run code which is stored as logs in S3 bucket for every DAG run.

This might help in backtracking and give information about the failures/runs happening for every run.

**Step 1:** Go to Okta portal, Open Amazon web services

**Step 2:** Go to below link and can see all the DAGs in here: 

<https://us-west-2.console.aws.amazon.com/s3/buckets/zendesk-dbt-artifacts-production-us-west-2?prefix=eda/2025/01/05/>

  * **Production/**




**Example:** Looking for **Fact_financial_bookings** compiled/run code

  * <https://us-west-2.console.aws.amazon.com/s3/buckets/zendesk-dbt-artifacts-production-us-west-2?prefix=eda/2025/01/05/Production/zdp_dbt_customer_financial_bookings/scheduled__2025-01-05T07%3A00%3A00%2B00%3A00/dbt_customer_fact_financial_bookings.fact_financial_bookings.run/1/target/compiled/customer/models/finance/marts/>

  * **Fact_financial_bookings.sql**




**Step 3:** Click the Download button to save the code to your local machine.

  *

---

## Access compiled sql dbt code and logs in ZDP

**Page ID:** 6787304227  
**Version:** 1  
**Last Modified:** 2025-01-15  
**Last Modified By:** Suhas Jangoan  
**URL:** [https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/6787304227](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/6787304227)  

We have two options to access the compiled code and logs for the sql model: executing the model locally or checking the AWS S3 Bucket.

## A. Steps to Get the Compiled Code Locally

  1. **Build the Model:**

     * Configure the model with **FULL_REFRESH** settings.

     * Retrieve the SQL from the `target/compiled` directory.

  2. **Build the Incremental Model:**

     * Specify the date for the incremental build.

     * Get the SQL from the `target/compiled` directory.




## B. Steps to Retrieve Logs and Compiled Code from AWS S3 Bucket

  1. **Access AWS App:**

     * Go to the AWS App in Okta: [Okta AWS App](https://zendesk.okta.com/app/).

  2. **Sign In:**

     * Sign in using the `okta/eda_team` role for the account: `zendesk-zdp-production` (Account ID: 265144930961).

  3. **Select S3 Bucket:**

     * Navigate to the S3 Bucket in the **us-west-2** region.

  4. **Locate the Required Path:**

     * In S3, go to: `zendesk-dbt-artifacts-production-us-west-2 > eda/`.

     * Select the appropriate **Year** , **Month** , and **Date** as needed.   
**Example:** `zendesk-dbt-artifacts-production-us-west-2 > eda/ > 2025/01/ > 06`.

  5. **Access Logs and Compiled Code:**

     * In the `Production/` folder, choose the relevant DAG folder (either scheduled or manual task) to retrieve the log for the compiled code in the target folder.   
**Example:**   
`Production/ > zdp_dbt_customer_adhoc/ > manual__2025-01-06T16:59:49.491724+00:00/ > dbt_customer_financial_bookings.fact_financial_bookings_run/ > 1/ > target/ > compiled/ > customer/ > models/ > finance/ > marts/ > fact_financial_bookings.sql`.




**Note:** The same steps outlined in section B can be applied to access the code and logs for staging from the AWS S3 Bucket.

---

## Customer Domain Data Modeling  (ZDP Foundational Layer)

**Page ID:** 6482395356  
**Version:** 12  
**Last Modified:** 2024-10-09  
**Last Modified By:** Suhas Jangoan  
**URL:** [https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/6482395356](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/6482395356)  

## Introduction

The Entity-Relationship Diagrams (ERDs) for the customer domain in SQLDBM are designed from an end-user perspective rather than a transformational perspective. These diagrams do not concentrate on the processes involved in transforming the data; instead, they emphasize the star schema data modeling approach. This design enables end users to efficiently utilize the fact and dimension tables for various operations such as queries, joins, and filters. 

_Example:__Bookings enablement document_

## Data Modeling Approach

The agreed-upon data modeling [approach](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1M9F5iR83QAxwKbbdJUVVicDJvjFDDB4v9hSa9rGEtNI/edit?usp=sharing) for the customer domain is the Star Schema. This schema comprises both dimension and fact tables, facilitating straightforward and efficient data retrieval and analysis.

**Pros of Star Schema dimensional modeling** :

  * Clearly defined methodology with ample documentation and training resources, and understood issues.

  * Data is clearly organized into stars making it easier to understand.

  * Conformed dimensions - adding new fact tables - e.g. new aggregation levels of existing facts - into star schema is very simple without having to replicate the dimensions.




### Fact Tables

Fact tables are central to the star schema and typically contain measurable metrics and mappings related to business processes. These tables can include multiple primary keys (PKs), allowing for complex data relationships and enhanced analytical capabilities. Fact tables store quantitative data for analysis and are often designed to accommodate large volumes of data.

### Dimension Tables

Dimension tables provide context to the facts stored in the fact tables. They contain attributes that describe the dimensions of the data, such as time, geography, or product details. Each dimension table has a single primary key (PK) and may utilize surrogate keys to establish relationships with fact tables. 

All of our dimension models are **conformed dimensions** , meaning they have the same meaning and structure across multiple data sources and data marts in an organization. It is used in data warehousing to allow for the comparison of measures across different business processes.

_Example: dim_crm_accounts_daily_snapshot dimension is used by multiple teams and fact tables (fact_financial_bookings, fact_financial_product_bookings etc)_

## Alignment with Data Governance on Naming of the Models

We have collaborated closely with the data governance team to establish standardized naming conventions for our models. This alignment ensures clarity, consistency, and ease of understanding across the organization. For further details on the naming conventions, please refer to the [Naming Conventions Document](https://docs.google.com/document/d/13k25uiWrxX0eAIsaoomappqKU_27ChNRUePq-b-OUfo/edit#heading=h.lvu1j05x5y2t).

## Master data Subdomain

In the master data subdomain, we capture attributes at each grain of a customer. The following dimension tables are established to reflect unique records active on a given day at various account grains:

  * **dim_crm_accounts_daily_snapshot** : Contains unique records that are active on a day at the CRM account grain.

  * **dim_billing_accounts_daily_snapshot** : Contains unique records that are active on a day at the billing account grain.

  * **dim_instance_accounts_daily_snapshot** : Contains unique records that are active on a day at the instance account grain. _(Maintained by prodev team, will need to be imported as a global model)._

  * **dim_instance_account_products_daily_snapshot** : Contains unique records that are active on a day at the instance product grain. _(Curated for OBP usecase, potentially ownership will be moved to proddev)._




{"userId":"63f7b66fce6f37e5ed94e55f","projectId":277873,"projectName":"Customer Data Domain","project":{"id":277873,"name":"Customer Data Domain"},"displayMode":1,"subjectAreaId":"e76b5730-71a7-466f-aa21-97b2117d3354","macrosHeight":600}

## Data Modeling Challenges and Solutions

### Challenge 1: Mapping Associations (entity_mapping_daily_snapshot)

We encountered difficulties capturing the appropriate mappings of how each CRM account was associated with a billing account and how each billing account was linked to various Zendesk instances. Additionally, there were different hierarchies within billing accounts.

**Solution** : A mapping table, or bridge table, was created to capture the mappings of the three grains in their appropriate hierarchies. The **entity_mapping_daily_snapshot** table now contains the mappings of the above three grains. This is used by various teams as a global model for getting the mapping of a customer across different grains.

### Challenge 2: Inconsistent Definitions of Market Segment (dim_crm_accounts_daily_snapshot)

The **market_segment** attribute is utilized across the organization by various teams, leading to different definitions for the same field. Note: market segments are assigned at the CRM grain.

**Solution** : We pushed this universal attribute to the foundational layer in the **dim_crm_accounts_daily_snapshot** and utilized it across various functional datasets to maintain a consistent definition. We collaborated with data governance to align all teams on the definition of the market segment.

### Challenge 3: Source Issues in Downstream Reports (dim_crm_accounts_daily_snapshot)

Source issues were identified in downstream reports, impacting data integrity and reporting accuracy.

**Solution** : By implementing dimensional modeling and creating dimensions for each grain, we are able to identify source issues earlier in the process. We are actively working to address these issues upstream to prevent any negative impact on downstream reports. For example, Salesforce calculated fields curation is now performed in the cleansed layer instead of the foundational layer.

## Opportunity Subdomain

  
In BigQuery, we previously had two Opportunity tables utilized by the Sales Force Automation (SFA) team and the Sales teams for Monthly Business Reports and Go-To-Market (GTM) reports: curated_bookings and curated_opportunities.

{"userId":"63f7b66fce6f37e5ed94e55f","projectId":277873,"projectName":"Customer Data Domain","project":{"id":277873,"name":"Customer Data Domain"},"displayMode":1,"subjectAreaId":"52a94c91-7eee-4365-971f-9fcae4c1d76c","macrosHeight":600}

In the new ZDP model, we have transformed these tables into the following:

### curated_opportunities is modeled as:

  1. dim_crm_opportunities

  2. fact_crm_opportunities

  3. fact_opportunity_lineitems




### curated_bookings is modeled as:

  1. fact_financial_bookings

  2. fact_financial_product_bookings




## Benefits of the New Approach

The tables dim_crm_opportunities, fact_crm_opportunities, and fact_opportunity_lineitems are part of the customer domain, as they are primarily used by Sales for GTM reports.  
The tables fact_financial_bookings and fact_financial_product_bookings belong to the finance domain, as they are utilized by SFA for Monthly Business Reports (MBR).  
Enhanced Data Quality Visibility:

The new structure provides better visibility into issues at different grains, allowing us to identify various data quality (DQ) issues. These issues have been documented in our design document, which can be accessed [here](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1rOaPgnMe96VFrcKrt2Y7uWaScadtK49_PxSTtj4nPrE/edit#bookmark=id.w4j9ox2rtsly).

## Reverse Engineering in SQLDBM with Snowflake SSO

**Page ID:** 6480789511  
**Version:** 1  
**Last Modified:** 2024-10-08  
**Last Modified By:** Suhas Jangoan  
**URL:** [https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/6480789511](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/6480789511)  

## Introduction

This document provides a step-by-step guide on how to perform reverse engineering in SQLDBM by connecting to Snowflake using Single Sign-On (SSO).

## Prerequisites

  * Ensure you have the necessary permissions to access SQLDBM and Snowflake.

  * You must be assigned the `SQLDBM_SERVICE_ROLE` in Snowflake. Currently, only specific users have this role assigned.

  * Coordinate with the Snowflake admin team to grant access to additional team members as needed.




## Step-by-Step Instructions

### 1\. Accessing SQLDBM projects

  * Navigate to the SQLDBM projects via OKTA.

  * Select the projects that you have access to, if you have any issues please request access.




### 2\. Select Reverse Engineering

### 3\. Click on Connect to DW

### 4\. Logging into Snowflake via SSO

  1. **Fill in Connection Details** :

     * **Server** : Enter `https://zendesk-global.snowflakecomputing.com`

     * **Role** : `SQLDBM_SERVICE_ROLE`.

  2. **Connect** : Click on the **Connect to Snowflake** button.




### 5\. Selecting Schema and Objects

  * After successfully logging in, you will be able to select the appropriate schema from your Snowflake database.




  * Use the filtering options to locate the specific objects (tables, views, etc.) you wish to add or update in SQLDBM.




### 6\. Select Upload Sql Script

### 7\. Adding or Updating Objects

  * **Update Existing Objects** : If the object you are selecting already exists in SQLDBM, it will be updated with the latest schema details from Snowflake.

  * **Add New Objects** : If the object does not exist, SQLDBM will create a new entry for it in the model.




### 8\. Find the added or Updated Object in Diagram Explorer

## Notes

  * Ensure that you collaborate with the Snowflake admin team to manage user roles and access effectively.




## Conclusion

By following these steps, you can efficiently perform reverse engineering in SQLDBM using Snowflake with SSO. This process allows for seamless integration and management of your database schemas.

## How to view market segments in Salesforce

**Page ID:** 6280446027  
**Version:** 5  
**Last Modified:** 2024-07-31  
**Last Modified By:** Suhas Jangoan  
**URL:** [https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/6280446027](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/6280446027)  

## Salesforce Navigation

To view the market segments in Salesforce, follow these steps:

  1. Navigate to the specific CRM account in Salesforce by inputting the `crm_account_id`.

  2. You should see a button or link marked "Assigned Territories" (as per the previously provided screenshot).

  3. Click on this link. It will take you to the "Assigned Territories" page for the account, where you can view all territories assigned to this account.




**Note:** Please be aware that any deleted territories will not be displayed on this page.

## Retrieving the Territories in Snowflake

To fetch the data for a particular account's territories in Snowflake, you can execute the following SQL query -

##   
FACT_CRM_OPPORTUNITY_DAILY_SNAPSHOT

Daily snapshots show how the data looked like at the end of each day of sales opportunities, designed for trend analysis and daily performance tracking, it facilitates the understanding of sales dynamics across varying time periods.

### Row Count Verification

Ensure that row counts are matching in dimension model and fact model.

  1. In DIM_CRM_OPPORTUNITY

  2. In FACT_CRM_OPPORTUNITY_DAILY_SNAPSHOT




### crm_opportunity_id 1:1 Mapping

Ensure that crm_opportunity_id maintain 1:1 relation in dimension model and fact model.

  * `run_date` : 2024-05-01

  * Count: 2,206,004

LEFT JOIN VALIDATION

RIGHT JOIN VALIDATION




## FACT_CRM_OPPORTUNITY_MONTHLY_SNAPSHOT

This table captures monthly snapshots from `fact_crm_opportunity_daily_snapshot` are exactly the same as daily snapshots, except we provide one copy of the data per month. Typically we'll use the latest version of the data for that month that we have available to represent how the data looked at the end of each month. The reason to actually provide them as a separate table is to simply and optimize downstream queries that don't need daily granularity.  
  
**REF** : <https://docs.google.com/document/d/1UAf7lsXxjGnD1sGnkomd1ypA0mV60ucEwychZWRU2iQ/edit#heading=h.hsc7ry6ogmpf>

###   
Mismatch Verification

Ensure that IDs are matching in Daily vs Monthly Snapshot tables   
i. for each end of the month run_date   
ii. capture only latest run_date data in monthly snapshot on daily basis  


####   
**1\. End of the Month**

  
`run_date`: 2024-02-29

Monthly Snapshot ID Count

Daily Snapshot ID Count

  * No mismatch found




Comparing Partitions

#### **2\. Latest Run Date**

`run_date`: 2024-03-01  


Monthly Snapshot ID Count

Comparing Partition for Recent Run

  
`run_date`: 2024-03-02

Monthly Snapshot ID Count

Comparing Partition for Recent Run

  
Monthly snapshot table captured data from daily snapshot table last date record from each previous month and current date records for latest `run_date` . 

**Test Cases**| **Description**  
---|---  
**Row Count Verification**|  No discrepancies in record count found from source. All Rows are matching in both Daily vs Monthly Snapshot tables.  
**crm_opportunity_id 1:1 Mapping**|  IDs are unique in both Daily vs Monthly Snapshot tables for the given `run_date`.  
**Mismatch Verification**|  Ensure that monthly snapshot table capture all records of daily_snapshot table on last date of each month as well current state for latest `run_date` .

## Discrepancy Analysis Queries

### Query to Find Discrepancies Between Snowflake and BigQuery for Mid-Market segment

sql

Initial analysis indicates that the `active_territory` values in Snowflake may not be accurate, leading to discrepancies when compared to BigQuery. Further investigation is required on why the active territories market segment are wrong in snowflake

* * *

Based on the provided valid to values for objects in BigQuery and Snowflake, it is clear that there is a discrepancy in the data between the two databases. Specifically, the 'obj_terr_valid_to' date for one of the rows from BigQuery ends on '2024-04-19', whereas the equivalent data in Snowflake has an end date of '9999-12-31' for the same object, indicating it is still valid indefinitely. This difference in the validity range of the data is likely causing the discrepancy in the row counts between the queries executed in BigQuery and Snowflake. Since the queries filter based on these date ranges, any variation in the data will directly influence the number of rows returned.

**SAAS RAW**

**Historical data migration**

This record wasn't touched in the migration process because it was already ingested by fivetran prior to the migration date.

upon further analysis, by importing the bigquery dataset of active territories into snowflake and comparing the results, it was observed that some records present in bigquery are not found in the corresponding raw tables of snowflake. this was determined using a query that performs a 'minus' operation between datasets in both environments, indicating a mismatch in the records. here's the query used to spot these discrepancies:

**Missing records in Snowflake raw objects**

The association for this object is missing in snowflake but exists in bigquery and salesforce

There are about 1k records missing in the association table

Support Call with fivetran

Issues identified - 

  1. records were not found in the deleted api endpoint, the fivetran support person showed us how to hit the end points and suggested a full resync based on data validation, how do we do the data validation? Create a validation script to create a count check and do a full refresh when there are discrepancies. 

  2. Schema was disabled in fivetran for all salesforce objects so we were not able to find records in the raw table -> Impact is on all objects not just the association object. Change via tf -> After the next sync we should be up to date 

  3. For future to itcrm -> avoid hard deletes

After full resync of the object --

Upon further analysis it looks like there is an issue with our scd2 snapshots, even though fivetran has updated the deleted flag to true, it doesnt update the timestamp fields so the record is still showing as active in our scd2 table where as in big query the same record has the correct dw_eff_end date.

**No issues** - the valid_to_timestamp is set to 2024-5-30 instead of 2024-4-18 (bigquery) because the full resync happened on 5-30, **we need to discuss on how to fix this issue.**

# **Records Mismatch Analysis**

Identify the root cause and origin of discrepancies for a particular date.  
`the_date` : 2024-05-07  
  
**I. PRO_FORMA_SUBREGION**

`PRO_FORMA_SUBREGION` shows 20 unique values in BigQuery whereas `17` unique values in Snowflake.

**S No.**| **UNIQUE VALUES**  
**BQ vs SF**| |   
---|---|---|---  
1| null| 12141| 555109  
2| West| 54314| 38122  
3| UKI| 41195| 34345  
**4**| **Southeast**|  29|   
5| South| 75702| 57065  
6| SSAC| 41748| 17879  
7| Other| 346448| 1224  
**8**| **Northeast**|  57|   
9| North| 46993| 42994  
**10**| **Named**|  3|   
11| Korea| 5202| 5113  
12| Japan| 11672| 6843  
13| India| 13315| 13161  
14| Emerging| 29372| 15810  
15| East| 67196| 50635  
16| DACH| 5052| 4374  
17| Central| 44066| 25126  
18| Brazil| 46302| 18174  
19| Asia| 51886| 23373  
20| ANZ| 29873| 13069  
  
Records pertaining to the `SouthEast`, `NorthEast`, and `Named` categories exist in BigQuery but are absent in the Snowflake output. Let's examining from the output to original data source.  
  
The `pro_forma_subregion` field is derived from the `owner.user_sub_region`, which originates from the `int__curated_crm_user` table as the `subregion_c` attribute, and is part of the `salesforce_user_role_attribute_c_scd2` record.  


A left join operation was executed between `dim_crm_accounts` and `int__sfdc_curated_crm_user`, with the join condition specifying `account.crm_account_owner_id` equals `owner.crm_user_id`. It is evident that the source of the discrepancy originates from this specific join.

  
To pinpoint the root of the problem, we should focus on `CRM_USER_ID`, as it serves as the definitive identifier for tracing discrepancies originating from the source table `CRM_ACCOUNTS`.

Upon reviewing the output of the intermediate model `int__sfdc_curated_crm_user`, we discovered that 19 `CRM_USER_ID` entries exist but are not reflected in the `proforma_crm_accounts`. 

**USER_SUB_REGION**| **CRM_USER_ID**  
---|---  
Southeast| 0056R00000AKqI6QAL  
Southeast| 0051E00000FqCi4QAF  
Southeast| 0051E00000DwmcjQAB  
Southeast| 00580000005srwHAAQ  
Southeast| 0056R00000AKse4QAD  
Southeast| 0056R00000ChkG0QAJ  
Southeast| 0058000000DHfXXAA1

**Named**| **0056R00000ALNp8QAH**  
**Named**| **0056R00000AKshmQAD**  
  
Let's verify the two `CRM_USER_ID` records specified for `subregion_c` = 'Named' in the source table `CRM_ACCOUNTS`. `CRM_USER_ID` is `crm_account_owner_id` in the source table `CRM_ACCOUNTS`.  
  


BigQuery Output

Snowflake Output

Hence, the examination reveals that the absence of expected records is the contributing factor to this discrepancy.   


**II.** **PRO_FORMA_SUCCESS_DIRECTOR_TEAM**

The field `PRO_FORMA_SUCCESS_DIRECTOR_TEAM` is derived from data pertaining to the `region`, `market_seg`, and `subregion`. Discrepancies in source tables are therefore the primary contributors to inconsistencies within this field.

##  Relevant data

**Backfilling window**| **local execution**| **staging execution**| **model**  
---|---|---|---  
1 month| 5 mins| -| dim_billing_accounts, XS  
4 months| 7 mins| 8 mins| dim_billing_accounts, XS  
6 months| 25 mins| -| dim_billing_accounts, XS  
8 months| 31 mins / 27 mins| 16 mins / 13 mins| dim_billing_accounts, XS  
1 moth| 50 mins| -| dim_crm_accounts, M snowflake warehouse  
  
##  Background

Provide context on a decision the team needs to make and include information about constraints and challenges.

##  Options considered

| **Option 1**| **Option 2**  
---|---|---  
**Description**|  Maintain backfilling jobs separately| Modify existing queries in prod  
**Pros and cons**|  Low impact on existing prod data models. Less development time. Additional jobs for backfilling Additional jobs for backfilling|  No additional jobs to maintain. Requires high testing, delaying the deployment of historical data High impact on existing prod models  
**Estimated cost**|  MediumYellow| MediumYellow  
  
##  Action items

Add action items to close the loop on open questions or concerns.

1 complete Run jobs in staging and record dag time duration. 2 incomplete Create stories for creating backfilling jobs.

##  Outcome

We have chosen option 1 to begin with and will eventually transition to option 2 if all looks good.

## Backfilling customer domain data

**Page ID:** 6170477137  
**Version:** 6  
**Last Modified:** 2024-04-24  
**Last Modified By:** Suhas Jangoan  
**URL:** [https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/6170477137](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/6170477137)  

### Scenario 1: Backfill Migration Data from BigQuery to Snowflake  
  
**Objective** : Migrate historical data for specific dimensions (`dim_crm_accounts`, `dim_billing_accounts`, `entity_mapping`, `dim_instance_accounts`, `dim_instance_products`) from BigQuery to Snowflake.

**Approach** :

  * **Consult with the Finance Team** : Understand how the Finance team has approached similar migrations by meeting with Samantha

  * **Data Transfer** : Use a data transfer service or write custom scripts to move data from BigQuery to Snowflake. Ensure that the data types and structures are compatible.

  * **Validation** : After migration, perform data validation to ensure completeness and accuracy of the data.




Option selected - rebuild from source as maintaining code 

### Scenario 2: Backfill Data When Adding a New Field

**Objective** : Update daily snapshots in L2 objects to include a new field, which requires backfilling data for a date range rather than a specific day.

**Approach** :

  * **Modify Existing Queries** : Adjust the existing dbt or SQL queries to accommodate the new field. This involves changing the logic to select a range of dates for backfilling rather than a single day.

  * **Create New Queries** : Alternatively, create separate queries specifically for the backfill process. This would keep the daily snapshot logic untouched but requires maintaining additional code.




**Considerations** :

  * **Maintainability** : Having two sets of queries (one for daily snapshots and one for backfilling) can lead to increased maintenance overhead.

  * **Complexity** : Modifying existing queries to handle both daily snapshots and backfilling can increase the complexity of the queries.

  * **Automation** : Consider using Airflow to orchestrate the backfill process. Airflow can dynamically adjust the date range for backfilling and trigger the appropriate queries.




### Scenario 3: Automating Backfill Processes with Airflow

**Objective** : Automate the backfill process to reduce manual intervention and ensure consistency.

**Approach** :

  * **Airflow DAGs** : Create Directed Acyclic Graphs (DAGs) in Airflow to manage the backfill process. The DAGs can be parameterized to handle different date ranges and datasets.

  * **Dynamic Queries** : Use Airflow's templating features to dynamically generate the SQL or dbt queries needed for backfilling, based on the parameters passed to the DAG.

  * **Scheduling** : Schedule the backfill DAGs to run at appropriate times, ensuring that they do not interfere with the regular ETL processes.




**Best Practice Recommendation** :  
Given the need to maintain two sets of queries if separate backfill queries are created, it is generally advisable to modify the existing queries to handle backfilling. This can be done by parameterizing the queries to accept a date range, which can be controlled by Airflow. This approach reduces code duplication and simplifies maintenance.

However, if the logic for backfilling is significantly different from the daily snapshot logic, or if the backfill is a one-time operation, creating separate backfill queries might be justified.

1falseleftrich1cb892ee3-7188-40b4-8cfd-33b66a740427Confluence:2083817226700v2_17bea679e75e29023d43b00240778516856f2e39b1d1b7f0a91373ad85510909-a=103589275&c=Confluence%3A2083817226&d=89433a84-d870-495b-939e-b120b7b35bb4&p=617047713789433a84-d870-495b-939e-b120b7b35bb41713882856147500

query 

  * Select Date range

  * Pick your records and run your query to select latest records in each partition, query explanation is below.

  * The `CROSS JOIN` happens first, generating a complete set of combined records between your date series and account data.

  * The `WHERE` clause is then logically applied to filter these records based on the date range conditions.

  * Finally, within each partition specified by the `PARTITION BY` clause in the `ROW_NUMBER()`, the function assigns a row number based on the criteria specified in the `ORDER BY` clause.

REF: [https://zendesk.slack.com/archives/C06K3PG2F9U/p1716299999097939?thread_ts=1715951088.207799&cid=C06K3PG2F9U](https://zendesk.slack.com/archives/C06K3PG2F9U/p1716299999097939?thread_ts=1715951088.207799&cid=C06K3PG2F9U)

This could also cause inconsistency in output of the derived `opportunity_meddpicc_score` field.

## Jira Story

<https://zendesk.atlassian.net/issues/?jql=text%20~%20%22CURATE-476*%22%20or%20summary%20~%20%22CURATE-476*%22%20or%20key%20%3D%20CURATE-476%20ORDER%20BY%20created%20DESC>

## Test Cases

### Source Data Verification

Ensure that the row counts for a specific `run_date` partition are consistent between BigQuery and Snowflake source data tables.

**Details**

The data is extracted for recent `run_date: 2024-04-10` to detect any inconsistencies that may have occurred in the source tables.

**== >** **BigQuery**

**S No.**| **Source Table [Big Query]**| **total_count**| **unique_count**

**Test Cases**| **Description**

**Source Data Verification**|  A huge discrepancy of records observed on total count and a large number of mismatch found for `run_date` which has been identified by the number of records in Snowflake vs BigQuery based on filtered dates for `dw_eff_start/end` vs `valid_to/from_timestamp` and it results in a huge discrepancies for each data value obtained for `run_date`:`2024-04-10` from source.  
**Cluster Key Verification**| `run_date` as a cluster key added to `dim_crm_territory`.  
**Validate Descriptions**|  Descriptions are added as comment to table definition.

## ZDP - Entity Mapping Analyst User Guide

**Page ID:** 6151569409  
**Version:** 7  
**Last Modified:** 2025-05-27  
**Last Modified By:** Suhas Jangoan  
**URL:** [https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/6151569409](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/6151569409)  

17flat  
  
# Overview

**Objective**|  The Entity Mapping table is intended to be a source of truth crosswalk table that houses relationships between CRM accounts, billing accounts, and instances.  
---|---  
**Current Stage**|  Core table prod v1 in zdp readyEnhancement to add smoochforce and stripe is in progress  
**Core table**|  prod_curated.customer.entity_mapping  
**Obtaining access**|  Email and request access from [data@zendesk.com](mailto:data@zendesk.com)  
  
# Sample Queries

**identify paying customer account hierarchy**

wide

**identify the level of a billing account within the billing hierarchy and/or identify instance, crm, billing ultimate parent, billing intermediate parent (if any) associated with an account**

wide

**identify all instance, crm, billing child accounts associated with a billing ultimate parent**

wide

**identify all instance, crm, billing child accounts associated with a billing intermediate parent in 3-level hierarchy**

wide

**identify all instance, crm, billing child accounts associated with a billing intermediate parent in 4+level hierarchy**

wide

**Identify billing account id counts by billing account source i.e. zuora/stripe-sunco/smoochforce**

wide

**Identify counts by billing account source for paying customers**

wide

## `immediate_parent_billing_account_id`

The purpose of the `immediate_parent_billing_account_id` field is to identify the direct, immediate parent account of a given billing account within the billing hierarchy. This allows you to keep the billing hierarchy consistent with Zuora's representation.

Importantly, this is strictly a billing hierarchy field and does **not** impact or alter the mappings between billing accounts, CRMs, instances (`instance_account_id`, `crm_account_id`, etc.). Those CRM and instance mappings remain unchanged and independent of this new field.

**View a sample of billing accounts alongside their immediate parents and related CRM/instance IDs to understand the relationships.**

### One Immediate Parent with Multiple Child Billing Accounts

This query shows all billing accounts where the `immediate_parent_billing_account_id` is `'8a1282cd8369bfb401838e2c71853b62'`, demonstrating one parent billing account with two child billing accounts:

**Count of Billing Accounts Grouped by Immediate Parent and crm_account_id**

### Note on Large Number of Child Billing Accounts for a Single Immediate Parent

While running sample queries on the `immediate_parent_billing_account_id` field, it was observed that the parent billing account ID `8a128b6184ae23470184c5b7243f65d9` has **1,635** child billing accounts:

Coy co

**Question:** Is it common or expected for a single parent billing account to have such a high number of children?  
Yes, that parent account corresponds to "Indigovern," which is a massive partner, so this is expected.

### Query to Find Billing Accounts Where Immediate Parent Equals Ultimate Parent

This query identifies billing accounts where the immediate parent is also the ultimate parent, which can be useful for spotting accounts at the top of their billing hierarchy or singleton parent-child relationships.

## Performance Issue remediation

**Page ID:** 6146228513  
**Version:** 2  
**Last Modified:** 2024-04-04  
**Last Modified By:** Suhas Jangoan  
**URL:** [https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/6146228513](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/6146228513)  

## Jira Story -  
  
CURATE-508cae89f0e-c846-3d65-88a5-bb277a2031b3System Jira

## Issue

concern was raised in data-curation-core-scrum channel 

<https://zendesk.slack.com/archives/C059B6BCQ1G/p1711545747435119>

  
I'd like to raise your attention to significantly increased execution time form 15 minutes to more than 90 minutes for [zdp_dbt_customer](https://zendesk.astronomer.run/dr7zivis/dags/zdp_dbt_customer/grid?dag_run_id=scheduled__2024-03-22T07%3A00%3A00%2B00%3A00) Astro job starting 03/23. As far as I can see all this increases were caused by adding DQ tests. I think you need to re-evoluate your test strategy to make it incremental and avoid running heavy compute tests on views.  
From my side we can talk if XS warehouse is not sufficient and it's time to scale it up to S or scale out and add one more node making it a cluster of two.

## Suggested Solutions

  1. Converting our intermediate models from views to tables could speed up our data processing. However, this change might lead to higher storage usage and increased compute load when dbt is building the models.

  2. We went through the dbt tests on our intermediate models and removed tests that aren't necessary. It seems we have several tests that are repeated across different intermediate models, We can reintroduce them on an as-needed basis for debugging purposes.

  3. The current schedule has the DAG running at 7 am, a time that might be contributing to the heavy load. We're considering moving it to 12 pm, which should help us avoid peak times.

  4. Given that an XS warehouse may not be sufficient for our needs, we should explore the possibility of dynamically resizing our warehouse to a Small (S) size during high-demand periods.

  5. Can we configure alerts either in Astronomer or Snowflake to notify us if the DAG runs longer than expected, even after these optimizations? This would help us quickly identify and address any new performance issues.

---
