## zdp_dbt_customer astronomer dag testing

**Page ID:** 6126404916  
**Version:** 2  
**Last Modified:** 2024-03-21  
**Last Modified By:** Shubham Kumar  
**URL:** [https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/6126404916](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/6126404916)  

61falsedisclistfalse

##   
Jira Story

<https://zendesk.atlassian.net/issues/?jql=text%20~%20%22CURATE-450*%22%20or%20summary%20~%20%22CURATE-450*%22%20or%20key%20=%20CURATE-450%20ORDER%20BY%20created%20DESC>

Following story is also attached to two more Jira tasks:  
1\. CURATE-425cae89f0e-c846-3d65-88a5-bb277a2031b3System Jira  
2\. CURATE-451cae89f0e-c846-3d65-88a5-bb277a2031b3System Jira  


##   
ZDP_DBT_CUSTOMER Orchestration

**CUSTOMER** dags are dependent on `salesforce_accounts_scd2` and `zuora_accounts_scd2` views, which are being generated from Fivetran orchestration:  
a. `zdp_dbt_scd2_fivetran_salesfoce`  
b. `zdp_dbt_scd2_fivetran_zuora`

Two `ExternalTaskSensor` have been added to validate the successful operation of `FIVETRAN` dags. These tasks run natively in Snowflake SAAS and replicate the final output in Snowflake Global in CLEANSED database.  


Views are built on top of the CLEANSED database to access the `FIVETRAN_SCD2` output, which is referenced as input to the customer model. These views are being updated before running the customer dags using `DbtRunKubernetesOperator`.   
  
Finally, three different dags namely `DIM_CRM_ACCOUNTS`, `DIM_BILLING_ACCOUNTS` and `ENTITY_MAPPING` have been triggered separately using `DbtTaskGroup`.   


**ZDP_DBT_CUSTOMER** **Orchestration**

## Test Cases

  
In Astro Staging environment, the dags has run successfully for two consecutive dates `2024-03-18` and `2024-03-19` .

The output tables are available in [Snowflake Global DEV_CURATED](https://app.snowflake.com/zendesk/global/#/data/databases/DEV_CURATED) database.

  
The following cases are considered to validate the Customer DAG run:

  * WHEN BOTH `SCD2_FIVETRAN_SALESFORCE` AND `SCD2_FIVETRAN_ZUORA` MODELS RUN FAILS

No dependent DAG runs   


  * WHEN __`SCD2_FIVETRAN_SALESFORCE` MODEL FAILS

No dependent DAG runs because `DIM_BILLING_ACCOUNTS` and `ENTITY_MAPPING` are dependent on salesforce and zuora table

  * WHEN `SCD2_FIVETRAN_ZUORA` MODEL FAILS

Only `DIM_CRM_ACCOUNTS` model run successfully because it only depends on salesforce.

  * WHEN PREVIOUS DAY RUN FAILS 

This testing has been done on a local environment by validating two consecutive dag runs. Models do not run on the next day due to previous run failure.

## Accessing SQLDBM Diagrams

**Page ID:** 6103500476  
**Version:** 7  
**Last Modified:** 2024-03-06  
**Last Modified By:** Suhas Jangoan  
**URL:** [https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/6103500476](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/6103500476)  

none  
  
For those who require access to view or interact with domain projects within SQLDBM, please follow the appropriate steps outlined below.

### Viewing Access via Confluence

If you only need view access to domain projects, you can directly access them from the ZDP Data Modeling page on Confluence: [_ZDP Data Modeling_](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/l/cp/jdUeedVX).

### Enhanced Access via SQLDBM

Should you require the ability to create diagrams, add comments or view the diagrams directly within the SQLDBM application, proceed with the following steps:

**Note for Modeler Access:** We currently have a limited number of modeler licenses (7 in total), which may require rotation based on usage. Consequently, there might be a delay in assigning a modeler license. Please consider this when requesting modeler access.

#### Step 1: Okta Integration for SQLDBM Login

To enable login to SQLDBM via Okta:

  1. Add your email address to the `sqldbm-group.yaml` file located at [_ZIG - sqldbm-group.yaml_](https://github.com/zendesk/zendesk-identity-governance/blob/7e147390659d057b2901ffcc00a9d9c9357dd04e/data/groups/composite/sqldbm-group.yaml).

  2. Create a Pull Request (PR) similar to this example: [_ZIG PR Example_](https://github.com/zendesk/zendesk-identity-governance/pull/17087/files). Please include either `suhas.jangoan@zendesk.com` or `niral.patel@zendesk.com` as approvers for the PR.




#### Step 2: Jira Task Creation

Create a Jira task with the necessary details at the following link: [_Sqldbm Onboarding_](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/browse/DA3DS-2220). For reference, you can view an example of a properly filled out Jira task in the screenshot provided.

It's important to clearly specify the project names and your role (viewer or modeler) within the task to ensure proper access is granted.

**Note for Modeler Access:** We currently have a limited number of modeler licenses (7 in total), which may require rotation based on usage. Consequently, there might be a delay in assigning a modeler license. Please consider this when requesting modeler access.

#### Step 3: SQLDBM Login

Once you have been granted access, log in to SQLDBM via OKTA.

#### Step 4: Access Projects from Dashboard

After a successful login, you can access the projects from the SQLDBM Dashboard.

Note: With view access you can comment on the diagrams to collaborate with the Project team. Right click to add comment and tag project owners using their email address. 

### Requesting Access to Additional SQLDBM Projects

  
If you already have access to SQLDBM but need to access a new project, you will need to create a Jira task requesting access to the specific projects. Please include the names of the projects you require access to and any relevant details that may assist in processing your request.

Create a Jira task with the necessary details at the following link: [_Sqldbm Onboarding_](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/browse/DA3DS-2220). For reference, you can view an example of a properly filled out Jira task in the screenshot provided.

It's important to clearly specify the project names and your role (viewer or modeler) within the task to ensure proper access is granted.

**Note for Modeler Access:** We currently have a limited number of modeler licenses (7 in total), which may require rotation based on usage. Consequently, there might be a delay in assigning a modeler license. Please consider this when requesting modeler access.

## finance_attributes - dim_crm_accounts

**Page ID:** 6095274141  
**Version:** 37  
**Last Modified:** 2024-03-14  
**Last Modified By:** Suhas Jangoan  
**URL:** [https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/6095274141](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/6095274141)  

16falsedefaultlistfalse

## Context

To facilitate the finance domain, we need to integrate additional CRM attributes into the `dim_crm_accounts` model within the customer domain. We will examine the existing logic from the finance domain and incorporate the new attributes into the customer domain.

## Reference Jira Tickets on usage of some attributes

DA3DS-2105cae89f0e-c846-3d65-88a5-bb277a2031b3System Jira <https://zendesk.atlassian.net/browse/DA3DS-2105>

## Existing Finance query - <https://github.com/zendesk/eda_da3_enrichment/blob/main/apps/da3_enrichment/models/domains/finance/hob_customer_attributes/eda_hob__crm_dim.sql>

We can examine each CTE independently and document the design to ensure alignment with the customer domain.

### Account CTE

The account CTE is responsible for selecting and transforming data from the source CRM accounts table. It enriches the account data with additional attributes by performing joins with employee range mapping and CRM industry tables. Below is a detailed documentation of the transformations and logic applied within the account CTE:

  1. **Selection of Account Fields** : The CTE selects a set of fields directly from the src__sfdc_acct_scd2 table.

  2. **Join with Employee Range Mapping**




This join adds the `range_group` and `range_clean` fields to the dataset, which categorize and clean up the employee range data from the CRM accounts.

  3. **Join with CRM Industry Table**




This join enriches the account data with an `industry_combined` field, providing a consolidated industry classification.

4**.Derived Owner ID**

5.**Primary Owner ID**

### Date Dim CTE

The cte `date_dim` serves as a way to create a limited subset of date dimensions for use in the subsequent queries. The supplied comments suggest that there is a practical and technical limitation with the number of partitions, which motivates a capping of the dates to the 4000 most recent days, presumably due to constraints in BigQuery.

#### Open Questions

  1. What is hob_start_date, and how is it determined ?

  2. Given the process updates data every 6 hours, what implications does this have for performance?

  3. If the restriction to 4000 partitions due to BigQuery's limitations, what is the approach in snowflake?




### Active Territory models CTE

The CTE active_territory_models is used to identify the SalesForce (SFDC) territory models that are active for each day within a range determined by date_dim. It filters for 'Active' territories starting from a particular date defined by the variable market_segment_2024_start_date.

  * Identifies active territory models per day.

  * Relies on date_dim CTE to provide the date range.

  * Starts from a date defined by market_segment_2024_start_date variable.

  * Assumes only one territory model is active at a time per SFDC constraints.




#### Open Questions

  1. Who**** defines**** the****` market_segment_2024_start_date` and how is it managed?




### CRM CTE

Comprehensive details of crm accounts

#### Open Questions

  1. Test Accounts logic owner: What constitutes a test account in the `account.test_account__c` and `account.type_of_partnership__c` fields, and are there industry-standard definitions or is this company-specific?

  2. Success Role and Experience logic owner - How are `success.role_name` and corresponding `crm_success_role_experience` levels determined, and what is their significance in relation to accounts?

  3. Competitor Grouping Logic owner

  4. Health Risk Type Grouping logic owner: How are health risk types grouped into 'Non-Controllable', 'Controllable', and 'Unknown', and what impact do these designations have on account management?




### ProForma CTE

The `pro_forma` CTE is essentially an extension of the `crm` CTE that introduces calculated market segment dimensions applying business rules to logically assign market segments to accounts.

#### Open questions

  1. How do we backfill this dataset if needed? 

  2. Who determines the value of this variable - {{ var('pro_forma_forward_looking_freeze_date') }} ?

## Jira Story

<https://zendesk.atlassian.net/issues/?jql=text%20~%20%22CURATE-440*%22%20or%20summary%20~%20%22CURATE-440*%22%20or%20key%20=%20CURATE-440%20ORDER%20BY%20created%20DESC>

## Test Cases

The objectives are to validate and verify that the migration of data from BigQuery to Snowflake has been conducted correctly, completely, and efficiently, while maintaining data integrity, quality, and consistency.

### Source Data Verification

Ensure that the row counts for a specific `run_date` partition are consistent between BigQuery and Snowflake source data tables.

**Details**

The data is extracted for recent `run_date` to detect any inconsistencies that may have occurred in the source tables. 

**Source Table [RUN_DATE]**| **Big Query** **Count**| **Snowflake Count**| **Difference**  
---|---|---|---  
**2024-04-18**| **920,361**| **920,359**|  2  
  
  * `run_date`: 2024-04-18

  * BigQuery Table: `SourceData.sfdc_acct_scd2`

    * Total Count: 920,361  


  * Snowflake Table: `prod_cleansed.salesforce.salesforce_accounts_scd2`

    * Total Count: 920,359




A discrepancy of count 2 has been identified in the number of records in Snowflake vs BigQuery filtered data based on `dw_eff_start/end` and `valid_to/from_timestamp`. It can be attributed to inconsistent records coming from source data and airflow DAG execution timing.

A discrepancy in the number of records has been identified in Snowflake. The expected count based on Big Query was `1045750` on `run_date: 2024-01-12` but `1045676` records observed in Snowflake. The observed counts during the audit ranged from three to more than three hundred records, with an average discrepancy of forty-four records and counting for these two months. Additionally, a drop in data is observed on `2024-01-13` (row count drop from `1045676` to `914939`) indicating a loss of approx. `130737` records in BigQuery and it is also reflected in Snowflake.

  
This trend of row count difference between BigQuery and Snowflake indicates a drastic change over a period of two months resulting in the variation of of 2500+ records.

However, this variance is anticipated and can be attributed to the slight differences in the timing of the airflow DAG execution and inconsistent data coming from Source Table.

Other fine grain validation is performed based on <https://docs.google.com/document/d/1_dEJ5izGNCUuCXcg9dsWixcZg_EBODogf86J275dbx8/edit#heading=h.m2ptzoumxm7z> doc. 

### Data Similarity Comparison

Ensure the degree to which datasets or elements within a dataset are alike.   
  
Data similarity for all columns at a time could not be captured as it shows variation across all `915540` records. To determine inconsistencies between BigQuery vs Snowflake output, separate data-type analysis is being done to estimate the similarity in records for `run_date: 2024-04-18`.

The min-max value for numeric column describe the data distribution and mean shows the deviation among the given sample distribution. The differences between min, max and mean for Big Query vs Snowflake describes the variation of numeric data for `run_date`: `2024-04-18`. In this analysis, a very small deviation could be expected but the absolute mean difference greater than `0.5` or `1` states a huge variance in data. For now, the absolute mean difference > 1 captures a large variation for columns like `crm_account_revenue`, `x6sense_6qa_age_in_days_sell`, `x6sense_6qa_age_in_days`, `total_number_of_seats`, etc.

     1. `run_date`: 2024-04-18

Summary  


**Test Cases**| **Description**  
---|---  
**Source Data Verification**|  A discrepancy of `2` records observed on total count and a small number of mismatch found for each `date` which has been identified by the number of records in Snowflake vs BigQuery based on filtered dates for `dw_eff_start/end` vs `valid_to/from_timestamp` and it results in a huge discrepancies for each data value obtained for `run_date`:`2024-04-18` from source.   
**Row Count verification**|  A discrepancy of 9 records has been observed on `run_date`: `2024-02-26` and for other run_date too. The cumulative count difference from `2024-01-01` to `2024-02-26` reached to approx. 2500+ records. It can be attributed to inconsistent records coming from source data and airflow DAG execution timing.  
  
Additional Validation has been done for 20 days in April 2024 showing difference of minimum 1 to maximum 131 records.   
**Uniqueness of PK**|  The `crm_account_id` must be unique for each `run_date`. No duplicates for the specified date should be present.  
**Column Count Verification**|  Comparing the number of fields between BigQuery and Snowflake to identify any missing/additional columns. 6 columns are deprecated from Salesforce table.  
**Null Value Verification**|  Consistency in handling null values should be checked, and DBT models should fail if nulls are present where they shouldn't be for `crm_account_id` using a macro.  
**Column Unique Value Count Verification**|  Consistency of count of unique values in a column in a given table between current date vs prior date on `crm_account_id` to detect any possible drop of records. The warning should raise if count of 1000 records dropped for a day.   
**Cluster Key Verification**| `run_date` as a cluster key added to `dim_crm_accounts`  
**Validate Descriptions**|  Descriptions are added as comment to table definition  
**Verify Incremental Strategy**|  Counts are consistent, indicating merge strategy is functioning correctly  
**Data Type Comparison**|  Data type matched for each column.  
**Data Similarity Comparison**|  Value mismatch is being seen for all datatypes. These inconsistencies are coming from Snowflake source tables that cannot be addressed directly. The SourceData record may be updated after running the DBT-BigQuery jobs and some of them could be addressed by Airflow-DAG execution timing for DBT-Snowflake.

  * **String -** Mismatch in string column records count is observed for `SUB_INDUSTRY`, `GLOBAL_ULTIMATE_DUNS_NUMBER`, `TERRITORY_ZIP_POSTAL_CODE`, `TERRITORY_CITY`, `TERRITORY_STREET`, etc.
  * **Numeric -**  
A huge difference of values being observed for revenue related columns like `annual_revenue`, `crm_account_revenue`, `total_addressable_spend_cs`, `total_addressable_spend_ee`. 
  * **Boolean -** NULL value mismatch seen in boolean column like `is_excluded_from_territory_assignment_rules`, `is_originated_from_lead`, `is_test_account`, etc. which does not exists in BigQuery but in Snowflake.
  * **Date & Timestamp - **  
Timezone UTC+00:00 matched for all timestamp columns in BigQuery vs Snowflake.

  
**Verify Transformation Logic**|  Counts are matching after transformation, indicating logic is functioning correctly.

##  Background

## Context

This document serves as a guide to leverage Astronomer within Customer Domain for scalable and efficient data orchestration. It outlines our approach to integrating Astronomer for Airflow Dags and identifies the required permissions for setup and operation.

## Access

Assuming that all of us are part of the group `zdp-dbt-write` we should have access to Astronomer by default. This [github doc](https://github.com/zendesk/eda_astronomer/wiki) serves as a guide if you are not part of the `zdp-dbt-write` group.

## Local Development

The EDA Data Platform team conducted a demonstration showcasing the method for initializing the local environment of Astronomer and testing DAGs. This setup is currently under development; it is being refined to incorporate the use of symbolic links. The corresponding pull request has not yet been merged.

Demo Video - <https://drive.google.com/drive/folders/123xenH2B_Z6iGjKxtBl84ByNiwBXQ1Ej>

It is imperative to select a DAG format that optimizes maintainability, performance, and clarity. Below are the proposed configurations along with their advantages and disadvantages.

## Leveraging Astronomer for CDD Data Orchestration

**Page ID:** 6074105979  
**Version:** 4  
**Last Modified:** 2024-02-15  
**Last Modified By:** Suhas Jangoan  
**URL:** [https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/6074105979](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/6074105979)  

## Jira Story

<https://zendesk.atlassian.net/issues/?jql=text%20~%20%22CURATE-369*%22%20or%20summary%20~%20%22CURATE-369*%22%20or%20key%20=%20CURATE-369%20ORDER%20BY%20created%20DESC>

## Context

This document serves as a guide to leverage Astronomer within Customer Domain for scalable and efficient data orchestration. It outlines our approach to integrating Astronomer for Airflow Dags and identifies the required permissions for setup and operation.

## Access

Assuming that all of us are part of the group `zdp-dbt-write` we should have access to Astronomer by default. This [github doc](https://github.com/zendesk/eda_astronomer/wiki) serves as a guide if you are not part of the `zdp-dbt-write` group.

## Local Development

The EDA Data Platform team conducted a demonstration showcasing the method for initializing the local environment of Astronomer and testing DAGs. This setup is currently under development; it is being refined to incorporate the use of symbolic links. The corresponding pull request has not yet been merged.

Demo Video - <https://drive.google.com/drive/folders/123xenH2B_Z6iGjKxtBl84ByNiwBXQ1Ej>

## DAG Format Design Proposal for Customer Domain

## Introduction

In the customer domain, when developing our data orchestration strategy using Airflow DAGs in Astronomer, we are confronted with several design options to manage our dimension objects. It is imperative to select a DAG format that optimizes maintainability, performance, and clarity. Below are the proposed configurations along with their advantages and disadvantages.

## Design Options

### One DAG per Subdomain

Given our current subdomains, which include Master Data, Opportunities, Contacts, Campaign and Operations, Advocacy, and Contracts, implementing one DAG per subdomain would lead to a total of six separate DAGs.

#### **Pros:**

  * Maintaining a smaller number of DAGs is generally simpler and can minimize maintenance overhead.

  * This design keeps related dimension objects grouped within the same DAG for better contextual understanding.




#### **Cons:**

  * Some subdomains, such as Master Data or Campaign and Operations, may be larger or more complex, potentially leading to bulky and unwieldy DAGs.

  * Dependencies within subdomains could become intricate, complicating the orchestration logic.




### One DAG per Dimension Object

An alternative approach is to designate a unique DAG for each dimension object across all subdomains.

#### **Pros:**

  * Reduces dependencies between tasks, as each dimension object is managed by its own DAG.

  * Enhancements or fixes can be deployed for individual dimension objects without impacting others.




#### **Cons:**

  * Managing an extensive number of DAGs can prove to be cumbersome and may increase operational complexity.

  * Could lead to suboptimal resource allocation and scheduling challenges.




### One Comprehensive DAG for All Dimensions

A single DAG could manage all dimension within the customer domain.

**Pros:**

  * Simplifies the overall DAG architecture by consolidating workflows into one unit.

  * Reduces the number of DAGs needed to be monitored, scheduled and maintained.




**Cons:**

  * May lead to a highly cluttered and complex DAG, with an overwhelming number of tasks to manage within a single workflow.

  * Increases the risk of a single point of failure that could potentially disrupt multiple data processes.




## Recommendations

It appears that the `One DAG per Subdomain` design offers a balanced approach, aligning simplicity with logical data grouping.

---

## entity_mapping_testing

**Page ID:** 6072401928  
**Version:** 10  
**Last Modified:** 2024-04-22  
**Last Modified By:** Bhavin Patel (Deactivated)  
**URL:** [https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/6072401928](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/6072401928)

## Jira Story

### **Billing_account_id to crm_account_id Mapping Validation:**

For this validation, we will be comparing finance table i.e. PROD_SAAS_CLEANSED.HOB_HIST.EDA_HOB__QTD_RECURRING_REVENUE_BUNDLED with PROD_CURATED.CUSTONER.ENTITY_MAPPING._

#### **STRIPE:**

There are 414 distinct billing account ids in finance against 11,371 distinct billing account ids in ENTITY_MAPPING. We are keeping all the stripe billing account ids while finance is only keeping those which has crm ids resulting in this volume difference between the two tables. As part of validation, we have checked billing_account_id to crm_account_id mapping in both tables using below query and got 5 mismatches (excluding 2 with crm_account_id like stripe%). Out of 5 mismatches, when we looked into one particular billing_account_id, it shows having two different crm_account_id associated with it on different days. So we can say that it is due to timing issue and will be fixed in latest run ( has agreed that this mismatch is fine because of timing issue and no further action is required).

**Query:**

select distinct billing_account_id, crm_account_id from PROD_SAAS_CLEANSED.HOB_HIST.EDA_HOB__QTD_RECURRING_REVENUE_BUNDLED  
where service_date='2024-03-21' and data_source = 'Legacy SunCo' and crm_account_id is not null  
and crm_account_id not like 'stripe%'  
minus  
select distinct billing_account_id, crm_account_id from feature_curate482.customer.entity_mapping  
where run_date='2024-03-22' and billing_account_source = 'Sunco-Stripe' and crm_account_id is not null  
and crm_account_id not like 'stripe%'

**Query Output:**

**Analysis of cus_JYysMNNer11O5m:**

#### **Zuora:**

There are 132,716 distinct billing account ids in finance against 504,703 distinct billing account ids in ENTITY_MAPPING. This difference is due to finance only keeping billing account ids with net MRR while we keep all billing account ids ever existed in Zuora. As part of validation, we have checked billing_account_id to crm_account_id mapping in both tables using below query and got 1.4k mismatches. But we need to exclude billing_account_id like zuora% (it was specifically done by finance team for their use case), which then leaves us with 52 mismatches. We have noticed a timing issue (similar to stripe) so if we compare next day entity mapping data with current day finance, we only get 3 mismatches. Again these 3 is expected to be fixed in next run ( has agreed that this mismatch is fine because of timing issue and no further action is required).

**Query:**

select distinct billing_account_id, crm_account_id from PROD_SAAS_CLEANSED.HOB_HIST.EDA_HOB__QTD_RECURRING_REVENUE_BUNDLED  
where service_date='2024-03-21' and data_source = 'Core Zuora'  
and crm_account_id not like 'zuora%'  
minus  
select distinct billing_account_id, crm_account_id from feature_curate482.customer.entity_mapping  
where run_date='2024-03-22' and billing_account_source = 'Zuora'  
and crm_account_id not like 'zuora%'

**Query Output:**

**Analysis of 8a12838d8e5bcecc018e628475091c20:**

We only have this in finance table and further analysis shows why entity_mapping doesn't have it. We are checking for 21st or 22nd March in zuora_account_scd2 only got this billing from 29th March and onwards.

**Analysis of 2c92a0f946dd1bac0146f261b2df518c:**

Comparing billing_account_id between finance table and entity_mapping shows we have null crm_account_id in entity_mapping compared to finance table:

Further analysis shows latest record in Zuora for this specific billing_account_id is having latest record with null crm_account_id. If we run entity_mapping for 29th Feb then we will have a record where crm_account_id will be populated. Considering a low volume for this timing issue, we can ignore this mismatch.

#### Smoochforce:

## Decision Log - Customer Domain ( Zendesk Data Platform )

**Page ID:** 6014468426  
**Version:** 8  
**Last Modified:** 2024-01-08  
**Last Modified By:** Suhas Jangoan  
**URL:** [https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/6014468426](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/6014468426)  

Decision-making within the ZDP program is distributed - teams are empowered to make decisions, or escalate them for cross-stream review based on the following principles:

## Decision-Making Principles

  * "Two-way door" decisions can be delegated, "one-way doors" (ie. decisions which cannot be easily un-made) should be made by our Steerco.

  * Decisions should be guided by our [target architecture](https://github.com/zendesk/techmenu/pull/905) and [transformation goal.](https://docs.google.com/presentation/d/1EJT-GDytW-dwrFp1YEm7o8LFFknkkMIfxl4NCwTQspE/edit#slide=id.g19616b92c85_0_468)

  * For delegate-able decisions, decision-making power sits with the [teams that own](https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1slUsmYjawP8u0E25eAS6fEIGBaPvH5nDenGajLBu7QU/edit#gid=0) the associated products/outcomes.

  * Decisions contained to one domain of ownership should be made by that team. Decisions with broader impact require buy-in from the impacted teams. "Broader impact" may include, but is not limited to:

    * Changes to operating cost.

    * Implications for system performance, security, scalability.

    * New constraints on the role or design of other components. 

  * If you're unsure - seek feedback! And if you need guidance, approach your Workstream Lead or Program Manager.

## Dimensional Data Modeling

**Page ID:** 5977049452  
**Version:** 5  
**Last Modified:** 2025-02-26  
**Last Modified By:** Tereza Cihelkova  
**URL:** [https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/5977049452](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/5977049452)  

Dimensional data modeling is a technique often used in data warehousing and business intelligence to simplify complex databases for easier querying and reporting. It involves organizing data into two types of tables: fact tables and dimension tables. This model is particularly favored for its efficiency in handling query operations and for the intuitive way it presents data, making it easier for end-users to understand and analyze.

  * **  Fact Tables:**

    * **Purpose:** These tables contain the quantitative data for analysis. Facts are typically numerical measurements or metrics.

    * **Characteristics:** Fact tables have a primary key that usually consists of a composite of foreign keys. These keys are references to the dimension tables.

    * **Examples:** Payments, Events, Transactions.

  * **  Dimension Tables:**

    * **Purpose:** These tables contain descriptive attributes or fields related to the business. Dimensions are the perspectives or entities with respect to which an organization wants to keep records.

    * **Characteristics:** They typically contain a primary key and a set of attributes. Dimension tables are used to describe objects in a fact table and are generally textual and descriptive.

    * **Examples:** Date, Accounts, Product




**Design Principles**

  * **Star Schema:** One of the simplest forms of dimensional modeling, where a single fact table references a number of dimension tables. It resembles a star, with the fact table at the center and the dimension tables radiating out.

  * **Snowflake Schema:** A more complex variant where the dimension tables are normalized, i.e., split into additional tables. 




**Advantages**

  * **Simplified Queries:** Due to its structure, dimensional data models can make data querying simpler and more intuitive.

  * **Improved Performance:** These models can lead to faster query performance, especially for complex and large-scale data.

  * **Ease of Understanding:** Dimensional models are often easier for end-users, such as business teams, analysts, to understand and navigate the data.




**Useful links and resources** :

  * [_dbt Discourse about Kimball dimensional modelling_](https://discourse.getdbt.com/t/is-kimball-dimensional-modeling-still-relevant-in-a-modern-data-warehouse/225/6) in modern data warehouses including some important ideas why we should still use Kimball

  * [ _Dimensional modelling manifesto_](https://www.kimballgroup.com/1997/08/a-dimensional-modeling-manifesto/)

  * [ _Dimensional Modelling techniques_](https://www.kimballgroup.com/data-warehouse-business-intelligence-resources/kimball-techniques/dimensional-modeling-techniques/)

  * [ _Kimball bus matrix_](https://www.kimballgroup.com/data-warehouse-business-intelligence-resources/kimball-techniques/kimball-data-warehouse-bus-architecture/)

---

## Finance data domain

**Page ID:** 5971641671

## Data modeling

**Page ID:** 5971641651  
**Version:** 20  
**Last Modified:** 2025-01-13  
**Last Modified By:** Tereza Cihelkova  
**URL:** [https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/5971641651](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/5971641651)  

Data modeling is the process of creating a visual representation of data domains that defines the information collection, organization and management of data from different source systems. Data modeling is performed in the [Foundational layer of ZDP](https://zendeskdev.zendesk.com/hc/en-us/articles/7990717076506-What-are-the-data-layers-in-ZDP). This data model helps different stakeholders, like business users, data analysts, data scientists, and data engineers to create a unified view of the Zendesk's data. 

#### Conceptual Data Model

The conceptual data model is the most abstract level of data modeling. It provides a high-level view of the system, emphasizing the organization of data without considering how it will be stored, created, or manipulated.

#### Logical Data Model

The logical data model is more detailed than the conceptual model, offering a deeper view of the data's structure and relationships. This model is more technical but still doesn't get into the specifics of how the data will be physically stored.

#### Physical Data Model

The physical data model represents how the model will be built in the data warehouse. It is the most detailed and includes all tables, columns, keys (primary and foreign), and relationships between tables.

Note, the below resources are outdated and do not fully align with the latest [ZDP layers](https://zendeskdev.zendesk.com/hc/en-us/articles/7990717076506-What-are-the-data-layers-in-ZDP). The below section need to be updated.

## Governance, Risk & Compliance Data

**Page ID:** 5971510530  
**Version:** 2  
**Last Modified:** 2023-11-22  
**Last Modified By:** Vijayakumar Janakiraman (Deactivated)  
**URL:** [https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/5971510530](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/5971510530)  

The Governance, Risk & Compliance data domain is the data responsible for ensuring that all corporate processes and procedures comply with the law or regulations.

---

## SqlDBM - Data modeling tool

**Page ID:** 5971510479  
**Version:** 11  
**Last Modified:** 2023-11-22  
**Last Modified By:** Vijayakumar Janakiraman (Deactivated)  
**URL:** [https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/5971510479](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/5971510479)  

SqlDBM is a Data modeling tool to streamline the process of developing effective and sustainable data models within Zendesk Data Platform, while fostering improved engineering standards and collaboration across different teams.

### [_SqlDBM Implementation Roadmap_](https://docs.google.com/presentation/d/1G42yWfhUubUS9cHNugOpfu0Ah8cLRtQfucc8CicE3Is/edit#slide=id.g25a838b9212_0_0)

**SqlDBM Links**

<https://sqldbm.com/Home/>

<https://intercom.help/SqlDBMhelpcenter/en/>

<https://academy.sqldbm.com/>

---

## Customer data domain

**Page ID:** 5971347192  
**Version:** 19  
**Last Modified:** 2025-02-28  
**Last Modified By:** Suhas Jangoan  
**URL:** [https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/5971347192](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/5971347192)  

Customer data domain is the behavioral, demographic and personal information about customers collected by businesses and marketing companies to understand, communicate and engage with customers or prospects. Customer data also includes any opportunities, contracts and customer support.

#### [_Customer domain L1-L2 dataset tracker_](https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1fK6XbKGdVtWyt9z_9q32lOJx_9JTejP7ITNI-mSPNnA/edit#gid=497609596)

#### [ _Dataset curation documents_](https://drive.google.com/drive/folders/17mjDyrveMpZOWGoA7hH2p65vTHa6GEti)

#### [ _L2 dataset design document_](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1tfUHy6MWtXWWlviHEIS8dfzB5kh2jpri4SHgLkXb5lk/edit)

#### [ _Customer domain pipeline details (legacy)_](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Egf2KEJPTu4S_o66niEXRCCuIViWFB0b4T4NBIMFFkw/edit)

#### _Sales & Marketing Sample Queries_

**Data modeling :**

#### [_Conceptual Customer Data model_](https://lucid.app/lucidchart/2f753afc-c76a-4168-9569-d7f75763660e/edit?invitationId=inv_26dec6d7-9e1b-4f06-b4c5-c92e1cd83fe5)

## Data Domains

**Page ID:** 5971281200  
**Version:** 9  
**Last Modified:** 2024-01-07  
**Last Modified By:** Vijayakumar Janakiraman (Deactivated)  
**URL:** [https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/5971281200](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/5971281200)  

Data is organized into domains to provide a common structure in order to clearly define boundaries, interdependencies and stewardship areas of responsibility. Below are the different data domains built as a foundation for supporting all Data and Analytics requirements.

**Data domains**| **Technical Implementation Owners**| **Notes**  
---|---|---  
  
  * Product 

| Foundation, ZAP, ED&A -  |   
  
  * Customer

| ED&A -  |   
  
  * Finance

| ED&A -  |   
  
  * People

| TBD|   
  
  * Vendor

| TBD|   
  
  * Governance, Risk and Compliance

| TBD|   
  
  * Reference

| TBD|   
  
Details of the data domains and sub-domains details are available in the below links,

[Data domain and sub-domains](https://society.zendesk.com/hc/en-us/articles/5072754382106-Zendesk-Company-wide-Data-Domains-Subdomains)

[Data domain Accountability matrix](https://society.zendesk.com/hc/en-us/articles/5330121727770-Zendesk-Data-Accountability-Matrix)  

[Data Governance Roles](https://docs.google.com/presentation/d/1p7K64jVYjCEV4vg5IVKuLLS0eW8fSjXxfYRfM2QyoNY/edit?usp=sharing)

---

## Zendesk People data domain

**Page ID:** 5971281187  
**Version:** 3  
**Last Modified:** 2023-11-22  
**Last Modified By:** Vijayakumar Janakiraman (Deactivated)  
**URL:** [https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/5971281187](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/5971281187)  

Reference domain is a special subset of master data used for classification throughout your entire organization. It can be used in data management to standardize and keep information consistent. Examples of reference data are postal codes, transaction codes, cost centers, financial / customer hierarchies, state or country codes, currencies, organizational unit types, language codes, customer segments, tasks and business processes

---

## Zendesk Reference Data

**Page ID:** 5971248459  
**Version:** 2  
**Last Modified:** 2023-11-22  
**Last Modified By:** Vijayakumar Janakiraman (Deactivated)  
**URL:** [https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/5971248459](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/5971248459)  

The Zendesk People data domain is data which enables the management of the employee life cycle (i.e., recruiting, hiring, onboarding, training, and terminating employees) and administering employee benefits, compensation, job performance and career development.

---

## Vendor data domain

**Page ID:** 5971216128  
**Version:** 2  
**Last Modified:** 2023-11-22  
**Last Modified By:** Vijayakumar Janakiraman (Deactivated)  
**URL:** [https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/5971216128](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/5971216128)  

Vendor data domain is information around complete records of the supplier's relevant information such as demographics, TIN, and contacts. Vendor data captures everything from procurement history to information about the goods and services sourced from the vendor, inventory data, contract records, purchasing records, and more.

---

## Template - Troubleshooting article

**Page ID:** 5961384521  
**Version:** 1  
**Last Modified:** 2023-11-09  
**Last Modified By:** Nicholas Nichson (Deactivated)  
**URL:** [https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/5961384521](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/5961384521)  

##  Problem

Add a short description of the problem.

##  Solution

Describe how someone would solve the problem in a short, step-by-step guide:

  1. Add steps that are simple and self-contained

  2. Add illustrations to instructions by typing /image

  3. Stick to 3-5 steps per task to avoid overloading readers




Highlight important information in a panel like this one. To edit this panel's color or style, select one of the options in the menu.

##  Related articles

The content by label feature automatically displays related articles based on labels you choose. To edit options for this feature, select the placeholder and tap the pencil icon.

## Template - How-to guide

**Page ID:** 5961384507  
**Version:** 1  
**Last Modified:** 2023-11-09  
**Last Modified By:** Nicholas Nichson (Deactivated)  
**URL:** [https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/5961384507](https://zendesk.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/ZDM/pages/5961384507)  

Explain what this how-to article is for. For example, you might write an article to teach people at your company how to set up a corporate email account or file an expense report.

##  Instructions

Create a step-by-step guide:

  1. Add steps that are simple and self-contained

  2. Add illustrations to instructions by typing /image

  3. Stick to 3-5 steps per task to avoid overloading readers




Highlight important information in a panel like this one. To edit this panel's color or style, select one of the options in the menu.

##  Related articles

The content by label feature automatically displays related articles based on labels you choose. To edit options for this feature, select the placeholder and tap the pencil icon.
